# 天皇至道太清玉册

**The Heavenly August Supreme Dao Great Clarity Jade Register**

**Scripture Title:** *The Heavenly August Supreme Dao Great Clarity Jade Register*. Compiled by Zhu Quan of the Ming. Two scrolls, nineteen chapters. Base text from the *Wanli Continuation of the Daoist Canon*.

**Preface to The Heavenly August Supreme Dao Great Clarity Jade Register**

How magnificent! How resplendent!

I say: the world has extraordinary men who accomplish extraordinary deeds. Without them, who could fathom the profound mysteries of the celestial Dao or plumb the abyssal depths of its source? Breaking through white clouds, grasping the azure vine, ascending emerald peaks, scaling layered ridges, traversing perilous cliffs of ten thousand fathoms, and climbing the summit of Mount Tai—looking down upon the earth below, one may deem oneself lofty. Yet who knows that riding the celestial winds as lightly as goose down, treading the rainbow as though straddling a blue dragon, roaming beyond the Great Void, touching the sun and moon, grasping the stars, licking the azure heavens, and gazing down upon the dusty world—how vast is such a spirit!

Unless one chews the blossoms of the Three Spirits, inhales the radiance of the Nine Lights, rinses the mouth with purple jade’s richness, and savors the true essence of primordial qi, how could one wander the spirit through the mysterious gate, ride the luminous winds of Langfeng, tread the azure void, and expound the celestial Dao?

Now, the composition of this book is like a divine chariot emerging from the vast sea or the rising sun dispelling the darkest night. It can cleanse the vulgarity of worldly dust and adorn the divine splendor of Mount Taihua. Thus, fixing the mind upon the numinous realm, one explores the Supreme Dao at the Celestial Ford; silently aligning with the Great Mystery, one grasps the divine pivot at the Purple Ultimate. For years, I have daily traced the sacred mysteries of the Perfected and probed the pivot of creation’s workings.

Herein, I dissect the unformed chaos before the division of heaven and earth, incise the primordial vastness before the Prior Heaven, reveal the hidden mechanisms of the Great Bird before its manifestation, and clarify the inception of the Great Simplicity in the generation of beings. From the undifferentiated state before the separation of the dark and light, down to the first emergence of human culture, since the establishment of the Daoist teachings—when the Three August Ones founded the ultimate principle and the Five Emperors received the mandate of heaven—those who revered the Dao and cultivated the celestial Dao: their teachings’ affairs were incomplete, their profound words unproclaimed, their institutions untransmitted, their rituals unrectified. I have therefore examined and renewed them. If not I, then who could accomplish this?

Thus, after thrice bathing and purifying, I pledged before the divine luminaries and reported to the Heavenly Thearch. I extensively consulted the classical texts, delved into every category, and thoroughly investigated all matters. Greatly proclaiming the mysterious transformation, I elucidated the initial separation of heaven and earth, the first division of creation, the inception of the Dao’s lineage, the forms of ritual, the preparation of implements, the systems of robes and crowns, rites and music, the profound mysteries of the celestial mind, and the regulations of the Daoist gate’s decorum. All were established as fixed standards. Whatever the Daoist gate employs is recorded in this book.

Thus, I name it *The Heavenly August Supreme Dao Great Clarity Jade Register*.

From the beginning of creation to the present day, across hundreds of millions of years, all who have possessed states or households have revered the celestial Dao above and cultivated human affairs below. Therefore, they built the Circular Mound to sacrifice to heaven and erected the Square Mound to offer to earth—all esteeming the celestial Dao. In every imperial decree, it is said: “Reverently following the mandate of heaven.” The *Book of Zhou* states: “Heaven above bestows its mandate.” The *Book of Tang* says: “The enlightened king reverently follows the celestial Dao.” Never has there been a time when the celestial Dao was not revered and the celestial mandate not received.

Alas! The mysterious wind has long been in decline.

Thus did I command the Dao’s ocean to surge its waves anew, stirring the mighty billows that strike the heavens; the divine radiance flared suddenly, once more dispelling the deep gloom of distant realms. Truly, one who gazes upon the towering waves that meet the sky does not seek their rise from a mere stagnant pool; one who beholds the vast and profound brush of the mysterious scribe does not expect it from the pedantry of mere phrases.

How could I dare to boast of myself? This book, rather, is like the thunderous roar that summons wind and storm, lashing the Azure Dragon to unleash the season’s rains; in its proclamation of the Dao, it soars through the celestial vault, riding the Yellow Crane to ascend the luminous void. In its system of rites, it is as though the numinous flute resounds in the cinnabar heavens; in its fashioning of things, it is as though the divine terrace bursts forth upon the Silver River. How magnificent is this renewal of the mysterious creation!

Therefore, I have entrusted it to the printing blocks, that all under heaven and future generations may know the greatness of the Heavenly August Dao to be as splendid as this—is this not wondrous indeed?

Written on the ninth day of the first month in the ninth year of the *Zhengtong* reign of the second *jiazi* cycle of the August Ming, by the South Polar Elder of Remote Longevity, the Emaciated Immortal.

*Composed by the South Polar Elder of Remote Longevity, the Emaciated Immortal, of the Primal Dao.*

The Emaciated Immortal says: Tracing the origins of the Daoist teachings, in the primordial chaos of antiquity, when the human Dao first emerged, the Mandate of Heaven was not yet complete. Our Dao Ancestor, the Yellow Emperor of Xuanyuan, inheriting the destiny of the Nine August Ones, rode the six dragons to govern the heavens, established the celestial pole on behalf of Heaven, and thereby fixed the Three Powers.

At that time, Heaven and Earth had not yet become luminous and distinct. There were no written characters, so knotted cords served in place of governance; no houses, so nests and caves became dwellings; no clothing, so bound grasses covered the body; no vessels, so cupped hands held water for drinking. Our Dao Ancestor, the Yellow Emperor, first created written characters, fashioned garments, built palaces, and crafted utensils—thus were the affairs of humanity made complete.

Now, among the Nine Schools and within the Three Teachings, the written characters in use, the clothing worn, the houses inhabited, and the vessels employed all originated with the Yellow Emperor’s innovations—all derived from the teachings of our Daoist school and the Yellow Emperor. Moreover, Laozi said: That which gives birth to Heaven, Earth, humanity, and the myriad things must itself have a source. He declared: “I know not its name, and so forcefully call it the Dao, and forcefully style it the Great—thus it is called the Great Dao.” Its teaching is called Daoism, and from this the world first received the name “Dao.”

By this reasoning, all who speak of cultivating the Dao or studying the Dao are but appropriating Laozi’s words to take “Dao” as their name—are they not disciples of Laozi’s lineage? Furthermore, Laozi’s words—“mysterious and yet more mysterious, the gateway to all wonders”—the very terms “mysterious” and “wondrous” were borrowed from revered names and employed in the scriptures, all using Laozi’s language.

Again, in the writings of Zhuangzi it is said: “Only after the Great Awakening does one know the sage.” The name “Great Awakening” was established by Zhuangzi, and later Emperor Huizong of Song took it to bestow the title “Golden Immortal,” using it throughout his scriptures—all derived from the books of our Daoist school and the teachings of the Yellow Emperor, Laozi, and Zhuangzi.

In ancient times, the Earl of the West attended Laozi with two youths, to whom Laozi gave the names “Auspicious” and “As-You-Will.” Later generations have all used these names, appropriating Laozi’s words—are they not disciples of Laozi’s lineage?

The teachings of the Yellow Emperor were to create and regulate all things to manifest the Dao of Heaven, serving as the foundation of governance. The Emperor himself declared: “To observe the Dao of Heaven and grasp the workings of Heaven—this is perfection.” As seen in the *Classic of the Yin Confluence*.

The teachings of Laozi, according to the *Er Ya* and the *Treatise on Arts and Letters*, were to “embrace purity and emptiness to guard the self, and maintain humility and weakness to sustain the body.” This is the art of the ruler facing south. It aligns with Yao and Shun’s virtue of yielding, and the *Book of Changes’* principle of modesty. “One act of modesty brings fourfold benefit”—this is its strength. Thus, to regard the state as one’s own body, and govern the state as one governs the self, is to “value the self above all under Heaven.” Only when one can entrust the self to the world may one be entrusted with the world—all these are the principles of self-cultivation, family regulation, state governance, and world pacification. As seen in the *Dao De Jing*, these are the Dao of China’s sages. Hence, it is called the *Orthodox Dao*.

What is the Orthodox Dao? China, dwelling at the center of Heaven and Earth, receives the upright *qi* of Heaven and Earth. Its people possess upright forms and upright voices. Their teachings do not employ foreign speech; they dare not speak unless it is the language of the former kings. Thus, there are no words of translation or false attribution. Their attire is not foreign; they dare not wear anything but the lawful garments of the former kings. What they wear are the robes and crowns of the Yellow Emperor, hence the title “Yellow-Crowned.” They do not mutilate their bodies, for “the body, hair, and skin are received from one’s parents and must not be harmed”—this is the beginning of filial piety. Those who attain the Dao ascend in broad daylight, soaring to Heaven to glorify their parents—this is the ultimate filial piety. They do not abandon their surnames, nor forget their kin, nor erase their ancestors—this is the filial duty of a child. In court, they observe proper decorum, practicing the rites of ruler and minister. As ministers, they serve the Supreme Emperor—this is the righteousness of a subject. They study the books of the sages and follow the Dao of the sages, adhering to ritual and righteousness. The principles of Confucianism and Daoism are one.

This Dao existed before the separation of Heaven and Earth, and its teachings were established in the era of the Three Sovereigns. It is not what Confucius meant when he said that later ages would have only recorders, and that heterodoxies would arise to distort the great principles. Among its followers, those of China are ranked above, while foreigners are ranked below. The teachings have distinctions of precedence, and people have divisions between Chinese and barbarians, as well as differences in nobility and baseness.

Among the Jurchen women who cultivate the Dao, they do not leave their chambers, do not gather in temples, and do not conceal themselves among men and women. Their clothing is distinct, and their teachings are free from perversity. They do not delude the world or deceive the people with doctrines of karmic retribution, misfortune, or fortune. They do not coerce others into donating their bodies or wealth as merit, nor do they act contrary to the Heaven that gave them birth or forget the land that bore them. Born in China, they uphold the Dao of China and do not forget their fundamental principles. Those who deviate from this Dao are not orthodox.

This teaching spreads across the Four Seas and is practiced throughout the world, beneath the utmost reaches of Heaven’s canopy and the utmost bounds of Earth’s support, within the light of the sun and moon and where frost and dew descend. Among all living people, the Dao they revere, the words they use, the clothes they wear, the dwellings they inhabit, and the utensils they employ—all were created by China’s sages, the Yellow Emperor and Laozi. Are they not all derived from our Daoist teachings?

The *Book of Zhou* states: “Within the realm, there are Four Great Ones: the Dao is great, Heaven is great, Earth is great, and the king is great.” Within the Three Realms, nothing surpasses these in greatness. Confucius said: “Those who know by birth are the highest; those who know by learning come next; those who learn through difficulty come after. As for methods of cultivation and action—these are not what the sages esteem.” Thus, they are not considered great. Is it not that the *kun* and *fei* trigrams existed at the beginning of creation, coeval with Heaven and Earth? Therefore, Daoism takes Heaven as its master. How magnificent is the Dao of Heaven!

I have seen books that seek to eradicate Confucianism and Daoism, which state: “In destroying the Dao, even the Jade Emperor of the Great Mystery trembles in the Nine Heavens, and the Celestial Worthy of Primordial Beginning loses his gallbladder atop the Three Clarities.” Such vile words swarm like bees, too numerous to transcribe. In attacking Confucianism, they claim: “The teachings of Confucius are of little use in governing the world, do not comprehend nature and destiny, and only address the present life. He may be called a worthy, but not a sage.” They further say: “Confucius’ name and status were no different from ordinary people. He merely transmitted the words of the former kings and had no teachings of his own—he was only a compiler, not the source of a teaching. What Confucius spoke were mere expedients to correct the world, and what Mencius spoke was merely to criticize narrow-mindedness. The Confucian school is base, nothing more than a trinket among the vulgar.” These are all books written using the script created by the Yellow Emperor, yet they turn against the Yellow Emperor’s teachings, slander the learning of Confucius and Laozi, insult the Heavenly Emperor, and exalt themselves. Is this not an egregious error?

Alas! Laozi said: “The superior person does not contend; the inferior person loves to contend. Only because he does not contend does the world have none who can contend with him.” The sage foresaw this long ago.

When I was eleven years old, still in childhood, I encountered an elderly woman in blue garments who said to me: “You must never forget your long-held aspiration. Only after sixty years may you be permitted to speak.” Thus, I now record these matters directly.

In the forty-seventh year of Shaohao’s reign, in the year *zhaoyang chifenruo*, I received the mandate of the Great Clarity to be enfeoffed as the lord of □□ in Hedong. By the thirty-first year of King Wuding of Shang, in the year *sangzhao yanmao*, 1,029 years later, I ascended to the Great Clarity and was specially advanced as the True Lord of the South Pole, the Subtle and Empty Dao, residing in the ninety-fourth palace of the South Pole. In Heaven, I served for 2,699 years. The Great Clarity bestowed upon me the Jade Seal of Penglai and the Golden Talisman of the Great Yang, commanding me to descend to the mortal world to rectify the Dao of Heaven, revive the mystic winds, grasp the numinous pivot, and unfold the transformations of the profound.

Thus, establishing merit across the Three Realms and inscribing my name in the Celestial Register—how magnificent indeed! Therefore, I compose this work. It reveals the profound mysteries hidden within Heaven and Earth, inherits the radiance of the sun, moon, and Milky Way. Where will-o’-the-wisps once raged, demonic glows instantly subside; as the mystic winds spread far and wide, the Great Dao unfolds and opens. The shadows of a thousand years, long shrouded in darkness, are once more illumined by the light of transformation; the lineage of the Dao, spanning ten thousand generations, is again continued in this present age. Thus is the Way of the sages of our Middle Kingdom made manifest.

With reverence, I take up my brush, burn incense, and inscribe these words before the lofty and boundless.

**The Venerable Elder of Longevity, Quxian of the South Pole, Subtle and Empty Dao True Lord, bows and writes.**

**The Jade Register of the Supreme Clarity of the Celestial-August Dao**
**Upper Volume**
**Composed by Quxian, the Venerable Elder of Longevity, True Lord of the South Pole, Subtle and Empty Dao**

**Chapter on the Opening of Heaven and Earth**

This Dao—those who attain it may transcend Heaven and Earth to exist alone, enduring through ten thousand kalpas without decay.

**The Dao of Heaven**
Quxian says: This Dao is that of which Laozi spoke: "Before the separation of Heaven and Earth, there was a thing, chaotically formed, born before Heaven and Earth. Vague and indistinct, silent and formless, abstruse and obscure, it cannot be heard. Compelled to give it a name, we call it the Dao."

The Dao is lofty beyond reach, profound beyond measure. It envelops Heaven and Earth, bestowed without form. Its source flows ceaselessly, empty yet never full. Constricted, it can expand; obscure, it can illuminate; supple, it can be firm. Embracing yin and exhaling yang, it unfolds the Three Luminaries. Mountains rise high by it; abysses grow deep by it. Beasts run by it; birds fly by it. Stars and constellations move by it. By it, non-being gives rise to being; the humble attains honor; retreat secures precedence. Thus, though unseen and unheard, from formlessness it generates form; from soundlessness, the Five Tones resound; from tastelessness, the Five Flavors arise; from colorlessness, the Five Colors emerge. Therefore, being arises from non-being, and existence from emptiness. By the principle of the One, it extends to the four seas and pervades Heaven and Earth.

In its wholeness, it is simple as an uncarved block; in its dispersion, it is vast as turbid waters. Turbid, it gradually clarifies; empty, it gradually fills. Serene as the great sea, drifting like floating clouds—seemingly absent yet present, seemingly existent yet vanished. The Weishi clan attained it to grasp Heaven and Earth; Fuxi attained it to inherit the Mother of Qi. The Northern Dipper attains it to remain unerring through the ages; the sun and moon attain it to remain ceaseless through the ages. Kunlun and Feng Yi attain it to roam the great rivers; Jian Wu attains it to dwell on Mount Tai. The Yellow Emperor attained it to ascend the cloudy heavens; Zhuanxu attained it to reside in the Dark Palace. Yuqiang attained it to dwell at the North Pole; the Queen Mother attained it to sit in the Lesser Expanse. None know its beginning; none know its end. Peng Zu attained it, living from the time of Youyu to five hundred years later. Fu Yue attained it to serve King Wuding, ruling all under Heaven. Riding the Eastern Ridge and the Tail of the Winnowing Basket, he ascended to become a constellation. Thus, Confucius asked Laozi: "Today, in leisure, I venture to inquire about the Supreme Dao."

Laozi replied: "Purify your heart and wash your spirit; temper your knowledge and refine your awareness. The Dao—how indescribably difficult it is to speak of! Let me tell you its outline. The luminous arises from the obscure; order emerges from formlessness. The spirit is mastered by the Dao, coming from boundlessness and going to no end. Without gate or chamber, it is vast and all-pervading. Its use does not weary the mind; its response to things is without limit. Heaven cannot but be high; Earth cannot but be broad; the sun and moon cannot but move; the myriad things cannot but flourish—this is the Dao!

If the Dao could be presented to others, then none would fail to offer it to their parents. If the Dao could be told to others, then none would fail to tell it to their siblings. If the Dao could be transmitted to others, then none would fail to pass it to their descendants. Yet it cannot be—there is no other reason: if the center is not mastered, the Dao cannot be known. If you return and seek it within yourself, the Dao is not far."

Confucius returned and remained silent for three days. Zigong, perplexed, asked: "Master, when you met Lao Dan, what advice did he give?" Confucius said: "Birds—I know they can fly; fish—I know they can swim; beasts—I know they can run. For those that fly, I can use a net; for those that swim, I can use a line; for those that run, I can use a snare. But as for the dragon, coalescing into form and dispersing into patterns, riding the clouds and ascending to Heaven—I cannot fathom it. Today, seeing Lao Dan is like seeing the dragon! My mouth gapes and cannot close; my spirit is disordered, and I know not where to dwell. What advice could I seek from Lao Dan?"

Thus, Yanzi praised the Dao of the sage: "The more one looks up to it, the higher it seems; the more one delves into it, the firmer it becomes. Gazing ahead, it is suddenly behind." This is the Dao of which Laozi spoke: "Look at it and it cannot be seen; listen to it and it cannot be heard; pursue it and its front cannot be seen; follow it and its rear cannot be seen." Such is the Dao.

Thus it is said: "August Heaven has no second Dao; the sage has no dual heart."

Therefore, I must straighten my robe and compose my countenance, raise my hands in a solemn bow, and offer a single word of counsel to the wise:

*"Beyond kalpas, fragrant responses are not far—*
*borne on the breeze into the jeweled chambers of immortals."*

If you recognize this intimately here, you need only this single word: *Dao*. If you lack the eye, you will but somersault within your nostrils.

Hah! I open my mouth to laugh for you, and unawares, white clouds arise over the western hills.

The primordial *qi* is a thing of undifferentiated wholeness, born before Heaven and Earth. It stands alone and does not change; it circulates without cease and may be called the Mother of Heaven and Earth. Before Heaven and Earth existed, its *qi* was chaotic as a hen’s egg, dark and moist, beginning to sprout. The vast primeval mist grew luminous, and the primordial *qi* of the Great Ultimate enfolded the Three as One.

*Ji* means "ultimate"; *yuan* means "beginning." The pure and light ascended to become Heaven; the turbid and heavy descended to become Earth. The harmonious *qi* became human; the motley *qi* became the myriad things.

In the time before Heaven and Earth divided, the primordial *qi* was blended as one—this was the Grand Beginning, the Grand Unity. As the *Daodejing* says: "The Dao gives birth to the One; the One gives birth to the Two." This is the primordial *qi* of the Great Ultimate.

The Great Ultimate arises from the Ultimateless. In movement, it generates yang; when movement reaches its limit, it becomes still, and in stillness generates yin. When stillness reaches its limit, it returns to movement. Movement and stillness alternate, each the root of the other. Yin and yang divide, and the Two Modes are established. The Two Modes generate the Four Images; the Four Images generate the Eight Trigrams. Creation is thus determined—this is the august title of Heaven’s principle.

*Ji* means "utmost extremity"; *shu* and *ren* are names for the root and foundation. This is what is meant by the pivot and hinge of Heaven, the root and foundation.

Once the primordial *qi* divided, yin and yang were distinguished. Soundless and scentless, the light and pure floated upward to form Heaven; the heavy and turbid sank downward to form Earth. Heaven moves with vigor, circulating without rest. The sun, moon, and stars are suspended from it, and the myriad things are covered by it. Heaven is vast, Earth small; their surfaces are enveloped in water. Earth stands upon *qi* and floats upon water.

Heaven’s motion is like the turning of a wheel’s hub, like a hat covering the Earth. Above and below, the primordial *qi* is as if a lidded box were pressed upon water to keep it from flowing—*qi* fills its midst. As the *Treatise on Heaven* says: "Heaven is round like a tilted canopy; Earth is square like a chessboard." Heaven revolves, half above the Earth and half below. The sun and moon, though moving eastward, are drawn westward by Heaven’s rotation into the sea, like ants on a millstone: the millstone turns left, the ants crawl right; the millstone moves swiftly, the ants slowly, and so they cannot but go west. Earth moves ceaselessly, like a person sitting in a closed boat who does not perceive its motion—such is the vigor of the primordial *qi*, floating and roaming without rest.

The *Comprehensive Mirror’s Outer Annals* says: "Heaven and Earth were chaotic as a hen’s egg. Pangu was born within it. After eighteen thousand years, Heaven and Earth split open. The clear yang became Heaven; the turbid yin became Earth. Pangu was within them, transforming nine times a day. He was divine in Heaven and sagely on Earth. Each day, Heaven rose a *zhang* higher, Earth grew a *zhang* thicker, and Pangu grew a *zhang* taller. After eighteen thousand years, Heaven reached its utmost height, Earth its utmost depth, and Pangu his utmost length. Thus living things began with Pangu, the ancestor of Heaven, Earth, and the myriad things. When he died, his head became the Five Peaks; his eyes, the sun and moon; his fat and marrow, the rivers and seas; his hair and beard, the grasses and trees."

It is also said: "Pangu’s tears became rivers; his breath, the wind; his voice, thunder; the pupils of his eyes, lightning. His joy became clear skies; his anger, overcast. Among the popular tales of the Qin and Han, Pangu’s head became the Eastern Peak; his belly, the Central Peak; his left arm, the Southern Peak; his right arm, the Northern Peak; his feet, the Western Peak. Only afterward did the Three Sovereigns appear. This is the beginning of Heaven, Earth, and humanity."

Numbers arise from the One, stand upon the Three, are completed in the Five, flourish in the Seven, and reside in the Nine. Thus Heaven is ninety thousand *li* from Earth.

The Measurements of Heaven and Earth:
The celestial body spans 357,000 *li* from east to west and north to south. Each quadrant measures 89,250 *li*. From Earth to Heaven is 80,000 *li*. Taking half the sun’s illumination of Yangcheng as the center, the body is perfectly round. The Southern Pole, seventy-two degrees, is hidden and unseen, forming the lower compass; the Northern Pole, seventy-two degrees, is visible and unhidden, forming the upper compass. Each degree measures 2,930 *li*, 71 *bu*, 2 *chi*, 7 *cun*, and 4 *fen*. In general terms, each degree is 3,000 *li*. Measured from below, each degree is as large as the sun’s disk at noon. Three hundred sixty-five degrees extend downward to the first layer of the Yellow Springs and upward to the starry heavens—97,200 *li*. From the lowest depths of the Nine Dark Abysses to the starry heavens is 12,180,000 *li*, as verified by the Yellow Emperor.

The Distances of the Directions:
The eastern extreme is where the sun rises; the western frontier, where it sets. The diameter between them is 200,023,572 *bu* and 72 *bu*. From the southern extreme to the northern frontier, the diameter is 230,500,075 *bu*, 75 *bu* less than the east-west span. These are the measurements recorded by Yu’s minister, Zhang Hai.

The Center:
It receives the correct *qi* of Heaven and Earth and fully embodies the transformations of the Five Phases. In Heaven, it is called the Five Stars; on Earth, the Five Phases; in humanity, the Five Constants. Thus when humans are born, their form and appearance are correct, their voices are correct. Therefore, the Yellow Emperor matched Heaven, and the color of the center is called yellow. His teachings took Heaven as their master—thus they are called the Heavenly Dao.

All emperors and kings who possess the world revere Heaven to receive its mandate, honor the Heavenly Dao to govern the world. Thus it is said: "They receive Heaven’s bright mandate and encompass the Four Seas."

The East:
The place where the sun rises, where the *qi* of generation resides. It governs spring and belongs to Wood. Its people are benevolent, called the *Dongyi* (Eastern Barbarians). The character *yi* (夷) contains *ren* (人, "person"), for they receive the clear *qi* of Heaven and Earth. The three mountains of Penglai and the ten isles of Fanghu lie here, so its people delight in longevity.

The West:
The place where the sun sets, where the *qi* of withering and killing resides. It governs autumn and belongs to Metal. Its people are fierce, called the *Qianghu*, *Quanrong* (Dog Barbarians). The characters *qiang* (羌) and *quan* (犬, "dog") reflect that they receive the turbid *qi* of Heaven and Earth. Ghosts and yin beings dwell here, so they delight in death.

The South:
The place of blazing brightness, where the *qi* of scorching heat resides. It governs summer and belongs to Fire. Its people are cunning, endlessly deceitful, called the *Tianman* (Field Barbarians). The character *man* (蛮) contains *chong* (虫, "insect"), including the *Miaoliao* and *Hu* tribes, for they receive the mixed *qi* of Heaven and Earth. The lands of shorn hair and bare feet lie here, so they delight in banditry and killing.

The North:
The place of accumulated yin, where the *qi* of severe cold resides. It governs winter and belongs to Water. Its people are brave, called the *Beidi* (Northern Barbarians), *Xianyun*, *Tujue*. The character *di* (狄) contains *quan* (犬, "dog"), for they receive the dark and gloomy *qi* of Heaven and Earth. The Khitan and Xiongnu dwell here, so they deem dying of illness inauspicious and death in battle auspicious.

The Sun and Moon:
The *Records of the Five Phases and Years of Emperors* states: After Pangu’s death, his left eye became the sun, his right eye the moon.
The *Classic of Mountains and Seas* states: Beyond the southeast’s *Mei* and between the *Gan* waters lies the land of Xihe. There is a woman named Xihe, wife of the Emperor, who gave birth to the ten suns.
Guo Pu’s commentary notes: Xihe is likely the one who first gave birth to the sun and moon in Heaven and Earth.
The *Classic of Mountains and Seas* further states: In the wilds of *Quanhuang*, atop Yang Valley, stands Fusang, where the ten suns bathe. Nine suns dwell on the lower branches, one on the upper, each containing a crow within.
The *Master Huainan* states: The sun is solid, a great luminous essence. Within it is a limping crow, called the three-legged crow.
The *Classic of Mountains and Seas* states: The spirit of Mount Zhong is named Zhuyin. When it opens its eyes, it is day; when it closes them, night. When it blows, it is winter; when it exhales, summer. Its body stretches a thousand *li*, with a human face and serpent’s body, crimson in color. It is also called the Torch Dragon. Heaven is incomplete in the northwest, lacking the ebb and flow of yin and yang, so a dragon holds fire essence to illuminate the Gate of Heaven.

The Moon:
The *Master Huainan* states: The moon is Heaven’s emissary, the cold *qi* of accumulated yin, long condensed into water. The essence of water’s *qi* becomes the moon. The moon is the east of yin, so when the moon wanes, fish brains diminish.
The *Master Lü’s Spring and Autumn Annals* states: The moon is the root of all yin. At the full moon, clams and oysters are full, all yin at its peak; at the new moon, clams and oysters are empty, all yin withdrawn.

Stars and Constellations:
The word *xing* (星, "star") means essence. The essence of the myriad things ascends to become the arrayed stars. It is also said to be the essence of water, or the essence of mountains and rivers ascending to become the arrayed stars. It is also said that yang essence forms the sun, and the sun divides to become stars—hence the character *xing* (星) is composed of *ri* (日, "sun") and *sheng* (生, "to generate").
*Chen* (辰) refers to the Northern Asterism, called the North Pole, where the *Chen* star resides as the pivot.
The *Comprehensive Calendar* states: The Lord of Earth established the stars and constellations.
The commentary to the *Astronomical Records of the Later Han* states: The Yellow Emperor divided the stellar lodges. There are 124 constantly visible stars, 320 with ancient names, and 11,520 faint stars—all created by the Yellow Emperor.
Yet the *Book of Rites* states that Emperor Ku ordered the stars and constellations. Thus, the Lord of Earth first established the stars, the Yellow Emperor named them, and Emperor Ku later ordered them.

The Northern Asterism:
The North Pole has five stars, with Taiyi always at the center—this is the Pole Star. *Chen* is not a star but the central boundary. When the Pole Star resides at the center, the arrayed lodges align, a pattern existing since the beginning of creation.

Stellar Lodges:
The *Genealogy of Emperors* states: Upon receiving the Mandate, the Yellow Emperor calculated and divided the stellar lodges to establish pitch standards.
The *Han Records* also states: The Yellow Emperor fixed the stellar lodges, as recorded in the *Erya*’s twelve divisions and twenty-eight lodges—all created by the Yellow Emperor.

Lodge Degrees:
Fuxi observed the patterns of the five stars and divided their approximate degrees.
The *Records of the Grand Scribe’s Historian: Treatise on the Calendar* states: The Yellow Emperor named the lodge degrees.
Minister Yan Zan said: Naming the lodge degrees means observing the degrees of the Three Luminaries’ advance and retreat to verify auspicious and inauspicious omens.
It also states: Emperor Wu of Han summoned masters of esoteric arts, and Tang Du divided the celestial divisions.
The *Han Shu’s Sound and Meaning* notes: He divided the twenty-eight lodges into bounded degrees.
The *Astronomical Records of the Jin* also states: Fuxi established the degrees of the celestial circumference.

Clouds:
The *Supplementary Exegesis* states: The *qi* of Heaven and Earth exhales to form clouds and inhales to form wind. Clouds are so named for their motion (*yun*, 运), rising when they strike stone.
Fog:
Water vapor ascends and overflows, becoming fog. It is also said that when the *qi* of yin and yang are disordered, fog forms. Or that when earth’s *qi* rises and Heaven’s *qi* descends in response, fog arises.

Rain:
When the *qi* of yin and yang harmonize, rain forms. Water descends from clouds as rain. Rain (*yu*, 雨) means to assist (*fu*, 辅), assisting and nourishing the seasons.

The Eight Winds:
The *Comprehensive Discussions in the White Tiger Hall* states: What is wind? Wind (*feng*, 风) means to germinate (*meng*, 萌). It nurtures things to completion, thus corresponding to the eight trigrams. Yang is established at five, reaching its peak at nine-five. After forty-five days, it transforms, and this transformation produces wind. Yin joins with yang to generate wind. Forty-five days after the winter solstice, the *Tiaofeng* (Regulating Wind) arrives. *Tiao* means to govern. After another forty-five days, the *Mingshu Feng* (Bright Multitude Wind) arrives. *Mingshu* means to welcome the masses. After another forty-five days, the *Qingming Feng* (Clear Bright Wind) arrives. *Qingming* means clear and sharp.

After another forty-five days, the *Jingfeng* (Majestic Wind) arrives. *Jing* means great, as yang qi grows and nourishes. After another forty-five days, the *Liangfeng* (Cool Wind) arrives. *Liang* means cold, as yin qi begins to move. After another forty-five days, the *Changhe Feng* (Gate-Closing Wind) arrives, signaling the time for storing and preserving. After another forty-five days, the *Buzhou Feng* (Unbound Wind) arrives. *Buzhou* means unjoined, as yin and yang have yet to harmonize and transform. After another forty-five days, the *Guangmo Feng* (Vast Desert Wind) arrives. *Guangmo* means vast, aligning with yang qi.

Thus, when the *Tiaofeng* arrives, the earth warms; when the *Mingshu Feng* arrives, all things are born; when the *Qingming Feng* arrives, the forms of things dry; when the *Jingfeng* arrives, thorns bear fruit; when the *Liangfeng* arrives, millet and grain ripen; when the *Changhe Feng* arrives, shepherd’s purse and wheat sprout; when the *Buzhou Feng* arrives, burrowing creatures hide; and when the *Guangmo Feng* arrives, all things lie dormant.

Therefore, the ruler follows and aligns with these winds: when the *Tiaofeng* arrives, light punishments are issued and delays resolved; when the *Mingshu Feng* arrives, borders are repaired and fields cultivated; when the *Qingming Feng* arrives, silks and treasures are presented to envoys sent among the feudal lords; when the *Jingfeng* arrives, the virtuous are ennobled and the meritorious enfeoffed; when the *Liangfeng* arrives, the earth’s virtue is repaid, transforming the four regions; when the *Changhe Feng* arrives, legal punishments are applied and granaries prepared; when the *Buzhou Feng* arrives, palaces and city walls are constructed; and when the *Guangmo Feng* arrives, capital sentences are carried out and judicial punishments enforced.

**The Celestial River (Tianhan)**
It originates between the *Ji* (Winnowing Basket) and *Wei* (Tail) asterisms in the east, called the *Tianhe* (Celestial River) or *Hanjin* (River Ford). It divides into two paths: the southern route passes through the *Chuanshuo* (Roving Fisherman), *Yuxing* (Fish Star), *Tianyao* (Celestial Key), *Tianbian* (Celestial Basket), and *He Gu* (River Drum); the northern route traverses the *Gui* (Tortoise), piercing below *Ji*, then through *Ci* (Silk), south of *Nan* (Southern Dipper), *Beikui* (Northern Ladle), and *Zuoxi* (Left Banner) to *Tianjin* (Celestial Ford), where it descends and merges with the southern route before proceeding southwest. It then divides again, flanking the *Paogua* (Gourd), threading through the *Renxing* (Human Star), *Chu* (Pestle), *Zaofu* (Charioteer), *Tengshe* (Flying Serpent), *Wangliang* (Wagoner), *Fulu* (Auxiliary Road), *Gedao* (Passageway), *Cidu* (Gate Tower), *Tailu* (Great Mound), *Tianchuan* (Celestial Boat), and *Juan She* (Curled Tongue), then turns southward, passing through *Wuche* (Five Chariots), south of *Beihe* (Northern River), entering *Dongjing* (Eastern Well) and *Shuiwei* (Water Level), then southeastward, weaving through *Nanhe* (Southern River), *Guanqiu* (Barrier Mound), *Tiangou* (Celestial Dog), *Tianji* (Celestial Discipline), and *Tianji* (Celestial Millet), vanishing south of the *Qixing* (Seven Stars).

Zhang Heng said: The *Jinhan* (Ford of Metal) is the qi of metal. Its root is called the *Shuihan* (Water Ford); when stars are numerous, there is flooding; when few, drought.

**Thunder and Lightning**
The *Huainanzi* states: When yin and yang clash and interact, thunder is produced; when they strike violently, lightning is generated.
The *Shuyi* records: Lightning is the Heavenly Lord and Jade Maiden playing *touhu* (a game of tossing arrows into a pot), their missed shots causing Heaven to laugh, thus creating lightning.

**Frost and Snow**
When the qi of Heaven and Earth congeals and condenses into dew, it becomes frost; when rainwater freezes, it becomes snow.

**Sleet and Hail**
Formed when yin and yang coerce each other, embracing yin within yang.

**Rainbows**
The unregulated qi of yin and yang, where pure yang assails yin. The male is called *hong* (rainbow), the female *ni* (secondary rainbow).

**Yin and Yang**
The *Chunqiu Neishi* states: Fuxi established Heaven and Earth, dividing yin and yang and the Five Phases.
The *Shiji: Lishu* records: The Yellow Emperor established the Five Phases, originating the five divisions.
Ying Shao said: They are metal, wood, water, fire, and earth.
Meng Kang explained: Heaven has four seasons, divided into the Five Phases.
Fire began with Suiren Shi. In high antiquity, people ate fruits, melons, clams, and oysters raw, which harmed their stomachs and intestines, causing many illnesses. The sage then drilled wood to make fire, teaching people to cook raw food into cooked meals. Thus, he was named Suiren Shi. He established platforms for teaching, created markets at noon, and introduced the ways of exchange, through which human sentiments were communicated. The transmitted books of later ages differ: the Grand Historian Sima Guang and Liu Shu record over a hundred clans spanning eighty thousand years, or twelve thousand years, or four generations—none can confirm which is correct.

**The Twelve Branches**
The Yellow Emperor established the twelve branches—*zi*, *chou*, and so on—to name the months, and also assigned twelve animals to correspond with them.

**The Origin of Humankind**
The *Fengsu Tong* states: Popular tradition says that when Heaven and Earth first opened, there were no people. Nüwa kneaded yellow earth to create humans. Overwhelmed by the task, she drew a rope through the mud and flung it, forming people. Thus, the wealthy and noble are made of yellow earth, while the poor and common are made of rope.
The *Huainanzi* says: The Image Emperor gave birth to yin and yang; *Tupian* gave birth to ears and eyes; *Sanglin* gave birth to arms and hands—this is why Nüwa transformed seventy times.
Xu Shen’s commentary: The Image Emperor was an ancient celestial deity who, when creating humans, generated yin and yang. *Tupian* and *Sanglin* are names of spirits. It also says: *Turen* (Sudden People) were born from the sea, *Turen* gave birth to *Ruojun* (Mushroom-like Beings), *Ruojun* gave birth to sages, and sages gave birth to commoners. The ordinary and mediocre descend from commoners, who trace back to the *Turen*—this is the beginning of humankind.

**The Year Star**
The planet Jupiter. When it descends among humans, it becomes a noble person. Dongfang Shuo was the essence of Jupiter; from birth, Jupiter did not appear, but when he removed his headscarf and flew away, the next day the Grand Historian reported that the Year Star had appeared—this was the event.

**Yinghuo (Mars)**
The Fire Star. When it descends among humans, it becomes a child, singing songs and playing games.

**Zhenxing (Saturn)**
The Earth Star. When it descends among humans, it becomes a woman.

**Taibai (Venus)**
The Metal Star. When it descends among humans, it becomes a strong man, dwelling in forests and foothills.

**Chenxing (Mercury)**
The Water Star. When it descends among humans, it becomes a woman, foretelling good and ill fortune, obscurity and prosperity, blessings and misfortunes—Heaven displays these signs.

Whenever a star descends, it must have a corresponding host.

**The Star of Numinous Efficacy**
When the Han dynasty ruled the world, Emperor Gaozu issued an edict commanding the entire realm to establish shrines to the Star of Numinous Efficacy, primarily for praying for abundant grain.

**Chapter on the Origins and Development of Daoist Teachings**
The origins of Daoism trace back to before the Great Beginning and Primordial Simplicity, to the time before the first stirring of the vast chaos. When Heaven and Earth were indistinct and the primordial chaos had just sprouted, there must have been a master of creation present within it, capable of initiating Heaven and Earth and establishing the Three Powers. At that time, when the sun and moon had not yet been born, mountains and rivers had not yet taken shape, and things and principles had not yet manifested, its image was vast and indistinct, as the *Book of Changes* says: "Before the ultimate, there was already a master governing it." Yet it was formless and nameless, remote and unfathomable—ultimately, its name cannot be known. Nevertheless, what is it that gives birth to Heaven, Earth, humans, and the myriad things?

Laozi was the first to reveal its mysteries, encompassing the Two Modes, and thus forcibly named it the *Dao*. That which opened Heaven and Earth and initiated the myriad existents must have had its spirit, yet its name could not be known—so it was forcibly named *Yuanshi* (Primordial Beginning). Hence arose the name *Yuanshi Tianzun* (Primordial Heavenly Worthy), the progenitor of the opening of Heaven and Earth.

According to the *Dongyuan Lingbao Zhen’gao Yuanfu Jing*, its summary states: In ancient times, before Heaven and Earth had divided and yin and yang had separated, within the vast expanse of primordial chaos, boundless and lightless, the Supreme One transformed through the Three Qi to give birth to the Three Realms. By the time of Lord Lao, scriptures and teachings were transmitted, and thereafter the ten thousand norms unfolded. The Heavenly Perfected Sovereign beheld the *Eight-Trigram Radiant Scripture* adorning the nine heavens with resplendent brilliance, transcribed it, and from this beginning, transmission commenced. Through the ages to the present, Daoist teachings have thus endured for myriad generations without end.

All emperors who receive the Mandate of Heaven are called the *Son of Heaven*. Thus, the son serves Heaven as a father. As the *Admonitions of Zhong Hui* states: "Revere and uphold the Dao of Heaven to eternally preserve the Mandate of Heaven." The *Day of Tai Jia* says: "The former kings heeded the luminous Mandate of Heaven to serve the spirits above and below." Therefore, receiving the bright Mandate of Heaven, they encompassed the Four Seas, above to uphold the Dao of Heaven and below to govern human affairs. It is also said: "Heaven bestows its Mandate," and "to receive Heaven’s Mandate and continue its work"—all these are acts of serving Heaven. Thus, their halls are called *Fengtian* (Serving Heaven), and their gates *Fengtian*. *Chengtian* (Receiving Heaven) is never spoken without reference to Heaven. Therefore, the Dao as a teaching takes Heaven as its master, and so it is called the *Fengtian Dao* (Way of Serving Heaven), known as Daoism.

**The Upper Three Sovereigns**
- **Heavenly Sovereign**: The Heavenly Sovereign of Jade Clarity’s Sacred Realm is Yuanshi Tianzun, also known as Pangu. In the time before the Image Emperor, within the empty and spontaneous void, a hundred thousand layers of primordial qi coalesced and transformed to give birth to the Wondrous Non-Being Sage Lord, who was honored with the title *Great Luo Yuanshi Zun*, the Effortless Spontaneous Wondrous Non-Being Supreme Emperor. Later generations called him the *Supreme Dao Treasure*, the ancestor of the myriad qi. In the time before the primordial image had manifested, this was the *Dao giving birth to the One*.
  - Another account states: Before Pangu, prior to the Great Beginning and Primordial Simplicity, that which gave birth to the Three Powers had a master of creation whose name could not be known—it was also called *Yuanshi*, yet distinct from Pangu.

- **Earthly Sovereign**: The Earthly Sovereign of Upper Clarity’s True Realm is Lingbao Tianzun, also known as the Earthly Sovereign. In the time before the distant kalpas of *Yankang*, at the beginning of the vast primordial chaos, a hundred thousand layers of true qi coalesced and transformed to give birth to the Wondrous Emptiness Sage Lord, who was honored with the title *Jade Palace Great Dao Lord, Wondrous Emptiness Supreme Emperor*. Later generations called him the *Supreme Scripture Treasure*, transmitter of scriptures and teachings, who initiated the norms of the Dao. This is the *One giving birth to the Two*.

- **Human Sovereign**: The Human Sovereign of Great Clarity’s Immortal Realm is Daode Tianzun, also known as the Human Sovereign. In the time of the Crimson Brightness and primordial chaos, a hundred thousand layers of Dao qi coalesced and transformed to give birth to the Wondrous Being Sage Lord, who was honored with the titles *Five Numinous Primordial Elder Lord* and *Hunyuan Supreme Dao Lord*, ancestor of the myriad teachings and Wondrous Being Supreme Emperor. Later generations called him the *Supreme Teacher Treasure*, who promulgated the Dharma and expounded the teachings, bringing the myriad images to completion. This is the *Two giving birth to the Three, and the Three giving birth to the myriad things*.

**The Middle Three Sovereigns**
- **Heavenly Sovereign**: The Heavenly Treasure Lord, born from the mysterious qi of Yuanshi, became the Heavenly Sovereign of the Middle Three Sovereigns.
- **Earthly Sovereign**: The Numinous Treasure Lord, receiving the primordial qi of Yuanshi, became the Earthly Sovereign of the Middle Three Sovereigns.
- **Human Sovereign**: The Divine Treasure Lord, receiving the initial qi of Yuanshi, became the Human Sovereign of the Middle Three Sovereigns.

**The Lower Three Sovereigns**
- **Heavenly Sovereign**: The Heavenly Sovereign is Taihao Fuxi, who ruled by the virtue of Wood. Born from the mysterious qi of Yuanshi, his title was *Donghua Perfected Azure Heaven Supreme Emperor*. Observing above and examining below, he received the *He Tu* (Yellow River Chart) borne by the dragon-horse and drew the trigrams, establishing images and initiating writing to open the myriad existents.
- **Earthly Sovereign**: The Earthly Sovereign is Shennong, the Flame Emperor, who ruled by the virtue of Fire. Born from the primordial qi of Yuanshi, his title was *Southern Culmen Vermilion Numinous Cinnabar Heaven Supreme Emperor*. He first tasted the hundred herbs, taught people medicine, and disseminated the hundred grains, initiating the way of food and drink.
- **Human Sovereign**: The Human Sovereign is the Yellow Emperor Xuanyuan, who ruled the world by the virtue of Earth. Born from the initial qi of Yuanshi, his title was *Taiyi Yellow Heaven Supreme Emperor*. He first created clothing, palaces, rites, music, writing, boats, carts, and utensils—thus the way of human life, food, and clothing was complete. The Emperor cast the Nine Tripods at Mount Jing, and when the elixir was perfected, a yellow dragon descended with its beard to welcome him. The Emperor ascended to Heaven on clouds and dragons with eighty-one female attendants and seventy-two ministers. According to the *Jade Calendar of the Grand Historian’s Astronomical Observations*, beneath the constellation *Willow* in the sequence of stars, there are seventeen stars of *Xuanyuan*—this is the verification. Thereafter, the Dao of alchemical ascension was transmitted to the world.

**The Supreme Lord Lao**
According to the *Sacred Records*, the Supreme Lord Lao resides above the Great Clarity’s Immortal Realm. He is the ancestor of primordial qi and the root of Heaven and Earth. Within the utmost stillness and emptiness, prior to the Great Beginning and Primordial Simplicity, he is the master who opened Heaven and Earth and gave birth to the myriad things. Governing the cycles of time and directing the movements of qi, he harmonizes essence and unfolds transformation, creating and destroying the Two Modes through countless kalpas. His emanations pervade worlds as numerous as motes of dust, beyond all reckoning. After the opening of Heaven and Earth, observing the world’s shifts between refinement and coarseness, he established teachings in accordance with the times, serving as the imperial teacher of successive dynasties, instituting laws and ordinances. Sometimes he descended from the Nine Heavens, sometimes he transmitted teachings across the Four Seas. From the Three Sovereigns onward, all emperors revered and upheld him. Thus, within the realms of Heaven above and Heaven below, all within the qi of the Dao are the transformations of Lord Lao. He has bestowed countless teachings, universally delivering salvation.

For the people employ it daily yet remain unaware—herein lies the enduring title bestowed by the Most High Lord Lao. Laozi is but a name; he is also called Dan, styled Boyangfu, and was the son of the Perfected One Li Lingfei. In the Zhou dynasty, those of great virtue were all addressed as "Father," as with Confucius being called "Nifu."

Yet Lord Lao the Most High is not to be confused with this Laozi. According to the *Annals of Shang*, Laozi was a man of Chu who first manifested at the frontier of birth in the seventeenth year of Yangjia of the Yin dynasty (gengshen, 1073 BCE). From the realm of the Great Clarity, he rode the essence of the sun, transforming into a five-colored pearl of mysterious yellow, large as a pellet. A jade maiden, napping in daylight, swallowed it and conceived. After eighty-one years of gestation, in the ninth year of Wuding (gengchen, 1191 BCE), he emerged from beneath her left armpit, already white-haired, and was named Laozi. Born beneath a plum tree, he took seven steps, one hand pointing to heaven, the other to earth, and declared: "Within heaven above, heaven below, and the Three Realms, the birth of heaven, the birth of earth, the birth of humanity, and the birth of the myriad things—all are the transformations of the Dao. Thus, only the Dao is supreme." Pointing to the plum tree, he said, "This is my surname," and so he was named Er, styled Boyang.

Born in the ninth year of Wuding (gengchen), he later greatly expounded the Dao. Posterity, witnessing the vastness of his teachings, came to address him as the Most High Lord Lao. *Jun* ("Lord") is a title for emperors and sages, while *zi* ("Master") is a general term for men. Thus, the Dao expounded by Laozi is none other than the Dao of Lord Lao.

As for his manifestations and descents before and after, they span countless generations, enabling him to establish models, institute teachings, and exalt the mystic wind for ten thousand ages. Later followers of his teachings also revered him as Lord Lao, though the uninformed mistakenly conflate him with the Lord Lao of the Three Clarities.

During the Shang dynasty, Laozi served as the *zhuxia* scribe under the Earl of the West. In the time of King Wu of Zhou, he became the Keeper of Archives. From the Shang to the Zhou, he lived for nine hundred years before ascending westward to Kunlun. As Sima Qian’s *Records of the Grand Historian* states: "None knew his end." Confucius called him Lao Peng, a worthy minister of Shang. Liu Dian’s annals confirm Laozi was a man of Shang—this is clearly recorded in the Confucian classics.

Yet texts that seek to erase the Dao suppress the account of Laozi’s departure from the pass to transform the western lands in the twenty-third year of King Zhao of Zhou. Instead, they shift his birth to the era of King Ding, while the *Comprehensive Mirror* records that by the time of King You, Laozi was already lamenting the Yellow River’s drying—King You being ten generations removed from King Ding, with Laozi’s name appearing across those ten reigns. Such distortions cannot be concealed.

Consider the *Wen Xuan*, compiled by Emperor Wu of Liang and Crown Prince Zhaoming, which cites the stele inscription of Wang Jianqi of Qi to expose the falsehood. This remains an unassailable consensus for all ages, making the sequence of events undeniable. The text states: "The two Zhuangs of Zhou and Lu personally witnessed the mirror of night’s radiance; the two Mings of Han and Jin jointly inscribed the brilliance of cinnabar and ink." The Five Ministers’ commentary notes: "The two Zhuangs’ birth and the two Mings’ rise are recorded in the Confucian classics, not in Daoist scriptures." Emperor Ming of Wei wrote a preface, and successive emperors composed eulogies—Laozi’s birth is documented in the annals, proof beyond dispute.

Moreover, the memorial of the Eight Scholars of Tang further clarifies the matter. How can one deceive others without deceiving the Confucian classics? Alas, the task is arduous indeed!

According to the *Biographies*, in the ninth year of King Zhao of Qin, during the reign of King Nan of Zhou, the Zhou dynasty declined. King Nan surrendered his lands to Qin, and the great Zhou revolution occurred. Laozi, knowing Qin’s brutality and that his Dao would not prevail, ascended Kunlun in the west, and his ultimate fate became unknown—this is the truth.

Zhuangzi attained Laozi’s Dao, mastering the virtue of divine illumination, grasping the mysteries of Heaven and Earth, understanding the cycles of destiny, discerning the principles of cosmic ascent and descent, and perceiving the mechanisms of order and chaos in the world. He told the Qi man Yu Zhen: "In one hundred fifty-seven years, the Zhou’s mandate will end." In one hundred seven years, during the jiayin year, Laozi, foreseeing Zhou’s impending fall to Qin and the obstruction of the Dao under Qin, must have gone into seclusion. Laozi was also called Lao Dan, and Qin Yi mourned him, calling out three times before departing—a sign that the Dao had perished. Thus, "Qin Yi" was taken as a personal name, with *yi* (佚) formed by adding *shi* (失, "loss") to the *ren* (人, "person") radical, meaning "Qin lost the man." Hence, it is said, "Qin Yi mourned him." The three cries signified: first, "My Dao is lost!"; second, "What am I to do?"; and third, "Qin has lost the man!" This demonstrates Zhuangzi’s mastery of the divine Dao.

During the reign of the First Emperor of Qin, Laozi descended at the Yi Bridge in Xiapi and bestowed the *Su Shu* upon Zhang Liang, naming him the Yellow Stone Master. In the time of Emperor Wen of Han, Laozi descended by the banks of the Shan River, known as the River Master or the Riverbank Sage. The emperor personally sought him, and the Most High granted him the *Daode Jing*. During the reign of Emperor Cheng, Laozi clarified and illuminated the scriptures. In the time of Emperor An, Laozi descended upon Mount Tai, named Jiang Xia, to stabilize the realm. Under Emperor Shun, Laozi descended to bestow the *Mengwei Secret Registers*. During the reign of Emperor Huan, he revealed the *Methods of Nourishing Life* and later the *Methods of Exorcism*. In the time of Emperor Ling, Laozi descended upon Mount Tiantai, transmitting to Ge Xuan the *Upper Clarity*, *Numinous Treasure*, and *Great Cavern* scriptures.

In the era of Chen Liu, King of Wei, Laozi descended in Lintao Prefecture of Longyou, telling Wang Shi: "The world will soon attain great peace." Later, during the reign of Emperor Ming of Wei, Laozi descended upon Mount Song, bestowing upon the Daoist Guan Qianzhi the *Yunzhong Chanting of the New Precepts*. In the time of Emperor Taiwu, Laozi descended upon Mount Song, commanding Qianzhi to confer upon the emperor the title of *Great Peace True Lord*, whereupon the reign era was changed to *Great Peace True Lord*.

During the reign of Emperor Yang of Sui, Laozi descended upon Mount Zhongnan, revealing to the mountain recluse Li Chunfeng the omens of the Tang lord’s mandate. In the time of Emperor Gaozu of Tang, Laozi descended upon Yangjiao Mountain, speaking to Ji Shanxing of the Tang’s imperial destiny and foretelling the completion of his enterprise in the fifth month. Under Emperor Gaozong, Laozi descended upon the Hall of Great Ultimate, where princes, ministers, and consorts all paid homage. He also descended at the Yangqing Temple. During the reign of Empress Wu, Laozi descended in Hao Prefecture, warning against her usurpation of the throne, and later at the Spring Brightness Gate.

In the time of Emperor Xuanzong, Laozi descended in Shu. He also appeared at the thoroughfare of the Five Phoenix Tower, revealing that the sacred talisman lay in Yin Xi’s former residence. Later, he descended upon the Qian Yuan Pavilion, which was then renamed the Pavilion of the Descended Sage. He also descended upon Mount Taibai and in He Prefecture, foretelling the omen of An Lushan’s downfall. Under Emperor Suzong, Laozi descended upon Yunlong Rock in Tonghua Prefecture. During the reign of Emperor Jingzong, he descended at the Grand Clarity Palace.

In the time of Emperor Huizong of Song, Laozi descended upon Mount Mao. Under Emperor Qinzong, he descended in Luoyang, informing the mother of Li Ruoshui that her son’s loyalty had moved Heaven and Earth, and the Celestial Emperor had elevated him to the ranks of the heavenly officials. Since the Jurchen ravaged China, transforming the Central Kingdom into barbarian lands, Laozi’s manifestations ceased.

From this investigation, the traces of Lord Lao’s transformations span myriad kalpas, his ascents and descents unfathomable, his comings and goings beyond measure. Successive dynasties honored him with titles and enfeoffments, bequeathing his teachings to emperors and kings for endless propagation—this is the true account of Laozi.

His teachings were transmitted to Zhang Daoling of Han, who became the Celestial Master, acting as Heaven’s emissary to propagate the Dao. The Celestial Master, the Boundless, Lofty, and Illustrious Great Emperor—his surname was Zhang, personal name Daoling, courtesy name Fuhan. A native of Fengyi in Pei, his lineage traced back to the Ji clan. The fifth son of Xuanyuan’s son Qingyang, named Hui, served as Bow Minister, inventing the bow and arrow and presiding over the worship of the Bow Star. His descendants held this office for generations and were granted the surname Zhang.

During the reign of King Xuan of Zhou, there was Zhang Zhong. Eight generations later, his descendant served as minister to Marquis Zhao of Han. His line continued with Ping, who fathered Liang, courtesy name Zifang. Liang served Han and was enfeoffed as Marquis of Liu. His son Buyi, Buyi’s younger son Gao, Gao’s son Tong, Tong’s son Wuwang, Wuwang’s son Liren, Liren’s son Jue, Jue’s son Qi, and Qi’s son Dashun—Daoling was Dashun’s eldest son.

In the tenth year of *Jianwu* (jiayin), the fifteenth day of the first month, he was born on Mount Tianmu in Wu. In adulthood, he entered Mount Longhu, compounded the Nine Heavens’ divine elixir, and received from the Most High the scriptures, registers, and secret texts, becoming the founder of the Mysterious Teachings.

The *True Records* in the *Daoist Canon* and *Divine Pivot* state: The Dark Emperor was once the son of Shaodian, who married the daughter of Mount Shu’s clan and fathered Gaoyang, known by his virtue as Zhuanxu. Zhuanxu’s father dwelled in the Weak Water region, his neck bearing the marks of pottery from the Seven Rivers’ ford—thus was he called the Dark Emperor. Wielding the trust of the myriad spirits, overseeing the host of deities to guide all things, he commanded the hundred qi, summoned thunder and lightning. Thereupon, he rode the chariot of primordial unity.

To the north, he patrolled the dark tombs of Youling; to the south, he reached Jiaozhi; to the west, he crossed the Flowing Sands; to the east, he arrived at the Coiling Tree. All beings in motion and stillness, all spirits great and small, all within the light of sun and moon—none were not under his sway. Traversing the four quarters of the earth, circling beyond the eight directions, wherever there were mountains of terraced towers or mounds of yin palaces, he transported the stones of Anxi to seal and fill them. He cast the bronze of Mount Yu into sacred tripods, each offering one to the divine peaks of Dongshan—not merely Mount Juqu alone.

This is what is called the Dark Emperor, as recorded in the *True Records*.

Moreover, according to ancient histories: In antiquity, the people and spirits followed separate callings. When Shaohao’s reign declined, the Nine Li disrupted virtue, and people and spirits became intermixed, their distinctions lost. Zhuanxu then commanded Chong, the Southern Regulator, to govern the heavens and oversee the spirits, and Li, the Northern Regulator, to govern the earth and oversee the people, restoring the old order so that none encroached upon the other. He first established the calendar, taking the first month of spring as its beginning—thus was he the founder of the calendar.

As the ages receded, though the *Daoist Canon* was gnawed by barbarian fires, the *True Records* still preserved its accounts at the margins, for even the Dao of Heaven has its abiding presence.

Furthermore, the ancient titles of Yellow Emperor and Dark Emperor refer to Xuanyuan, the Yellow Emperor, and Zhuanxu, the Dark Emperor.

**The Old Man Star of the Southern Pole**
Gonggong’s son, Gou Longshuang, attained the Dao and lived for over a thousand years. Ascending to dwell at the Southern Pole as the Longevity Star, it lies 143 degrees from the pole, entering the Well Mansion at three degrees, south of the Bow and Arrow stars—also called the Southern Pole. It regularly appears at dawn during the autumn equinox in the *bing* direction and sets at dusk during the spring equinox in the *ding* direction. It is customarily observed at the southern suburbs during the autumn equinox; when bright and large, it presides over longevity and prosperity. It governs the lifespan of all living people under Heaven.

Since the Northern Pole resides in *chou-gen*, the Southern Pole lies in *wei-kun*. The Southern Pole sinks 36 degrees below the earth, where it cannot be seen. Thus, its spirit emerges from the earth to appear in the south, called the Old Man of the Southern Pole. Yet its emergence is not always complete, so its appearances are irregular. When seen, it is auspicious, its power and position equal in majesty. Aligned with the Central Dipper, it assists the Supreme Emperor. Though south of the Well Mansion, it does not belong to its sequence. It is regularly sacrificed to on the second day of the second month with great offerings, and on the twenty-sixth day of the eighth month, it descends to the human realm to extend the lives of the virtuous—so records the *Treatise on Astronomy*.

**Southern Lineage**
Beginning in the Han, it was initiated by Lutang Zhao Sheng, Huayang Li Ya, Zhongli Quan, Lü Yan, Liu Haichan, Zhang Ziyang, Chongzhao Wang, Ma Ziran, Shi Xinglin, Xue Daoguang, Chen Niewan, and Bai Yuchan.

**Northern Lineage**
Beginning in the Song, Wang Chongyang journeyed to the Eastern Sea and saw seven golden lotuses in the sea. His master said: "Here, seven perfected beings shall emerge." Thereupon, he ordained Qiu, Liu, Tan, Ma, Hao, Wang, and Sun—the Seven Perfected. The Quanzhen teachings began from this.

**The Dragon Script of the Heavenly Sovereign**
**Register of the Three Caverns’ Scriptures and Catalogs in the *Daoist Canon***

From the time the Yellow Emperor expounded the Dao and Laozi transmitted the scriptures, through the rise and fall of a hundred million years up to the Song, the *Daoist Canon* comprised 1,881,500 scrolls. After the barbarian fires, only 5,134 scrolls remain.

In the time of the Jin and Mongol barbarians, during the decline of the Song, a Qiang man named Huyan Mai, envious that the *Daoist Canon* contained such texts as the *Scripture of the Moon Hidden in Heaven*, the *Jade Latitude*, and the *Nine Heavens*—all supremely secret books of the highest heavens—conspired with the barbarian ruler Möngke Khan of the Mongols to have them all burned and destroyed.

Here is the translation:

---

Its decree proclaimed: "The Han people shall promote the teachings of the Han, and the Mongols must promote the teachings of the Mongols. How can the scriptures of the Han surpass those of our Mongols? Any book or single character found shall be swiftly burned and destroyed, leaving no trace for inquiry." Thus, they were cut off and left untransmitted. If any copies remain, they have not entered the *Daoist Canon*. Now, under the radiant heavens of our Great Ming, the people of China must honor the Dao of China. Therefore, their titles are recorded below:

Liu Ji said: "Xiang Mai and others of the Yuan, envious of the scriptures of China’s Daoist teachings—books of celestial chapters and dragon scripts, treasures in jade cases and gemmed bamboo slips—when scholars of the time greatly esteemed them, and seven or eight out of ten Buddhists turned to the Dao, conspired with the Mongol ruler Möngke Khan to burn all the Chinese *Daoist Canon* scriptures. Their decree proclaimed: 'Whoever dares to keep even a fragment or a single character shall not be pardoned.' From then on, the *Daoist Canon* of China was severed. This occurred when the Song faced collapse, the barbarians ravaged China, light gave way to darkness, and the obscure encroached upon the bright—such was the cause.

From the Jingkang era, when Emperors Huizong and Qinzong were captured in the north, during the chaos of the Jurchen Jin’s invasion of China, the Qiang barbarians arose and destroyed the great Daoist books of China. Over the 272 years of the Yuan dynasty, they produced ninety volumes of heretical texts, falsely attributing them to Tang figures like Daoxuan, Daoshi, Xuanyi, Zhisheng, and Falin, thereby eradicating China’s Dao. Their *Record of Exposing Falsehoods* states: 'It would make the Jade Emperor of the Great Luo tremble in fear within the Nine Heavens, the Celestial Worthy of Primordial Beginning lose his gall atop the Three Clarities, the Lords of the Myriad Heavens blush in shame, and the Immortals of the Nine Palaces grovel in humiliation. They slander the Heavenly Emperor, obliterate Confucius and Laozi, and vilify the Yellow Emperor’s deeds—words too numerous to record.'

Yet the Yellow Emperor was the founding ancestor who established the ultimate under heaven, and Laozi was the ancestor of the Tang. How could people of that time destroy the ancestor of their own sovereign? How could the Chinese people destroy the Dao of China? In truth, these were the works of the Khitan Liao, Jurchen Jin, and Mongol Yuan. During the Duanping era of Emperor Lizong of the Song, when the barbarian bandits raided the borders, one or two volumes of these books were obtained. The emperor, upon reading them, sighed: 'Even with a hundred thousand volumes, the superiority or inferiority of China’s Dao versus that of the barbarians is evident without debate.' Thus, the titles of the heretical books that destroyed the Dao are recorded below:

*The Veritable Record of the Balance Between Buddhism and Daoism* (4 scrolls),
*The Continued Balance Between Buddhism and Daoism* (1 scroll),
*The Treatise on Discerning Orthodoxy* (3 scrolls),
*The Treatise on Debating Orthodoxy* (8 scrolls),
*The Treatise on Destroying Heresy* (2 scrolls)..."

*The Hongming Collection* (14 scrolls),
*The Expanded Hongming Collection* (30 scrolls),
*The Dharma Garden Pearl Grove*, Volume 55,
*The Zhiyuan Record of Exposing Falsehoods* (5 scrolls),
*The Comprehensive Record of Buddhas and Patriarchs* (22 scrolls).

**Zhengyi Registers of All Grades**
*The Supreme Zhengyi Alliance of Might and Perfection Register for Cultivating Truth and Extending Life* (1 set, 3 scrolls).
In total, twenty-four grades. This register subdues the myriad demons, elevates the nine generations of ancestors, welcomes perfected immortals at humble doors, and summons the ranked sages in the Jasper Capital. It advances ranks, elevates positions, rewards merit with promotion, and responds with manifest efficacy to those who reverently uphold it.

*The Supreme Register of the Three-Five Capital Merit Certificates* (1 grade).
This register’s grade may advance one to the immortal ranks, shielding the body from all perverse qi. Those newly entering the truth should first receive and wear it.

*The Supreme Register of Ascending Perfection and Esoteric Inner Teachings* (1 grade).
*The Supreme Register of the Purple Void and Natural Mystery* (1 grade).
These two registers conceal the hidden taboos of all heavens and assist the mysterious pivot of the Eight Sceneries. Through them, one may chew the Great Harmony, chant the Empty Cavern, diligently cultivate the wondrous Dao, and ultimately attain the immortal ranks.

*The Supreme Register of the Seven Primes of the Central Heaven Northern Dipper* (1 grade).
This register encompasses the profound purport of the turning jade mechanism and operates the mysterious pivot of the Dipper’s extremity. It nurtures and transforms all living beings. Those who receive and wear it with utmost sincerity will witness great blessings arrive in abundance.

*The Supreme Register of Moving Mountains and Breaking Earth: The Nine Oxen* (1 grade).
This register enables the relocation of graves and establishment of dwellings, subjugating earth spirits. It transforms the thirty-six malevolent forces into auspicious omens and causes the twenty-four directions to offer felicitous signs. It is a profound technique that universally aids all people.

*The Supreme Register of the Dark Heaven Perfected Warrior, the Peerless General* (1 grade).
This register conceals the inner talismans of the Void and Danger constellations and harbors the primordial essence of water and fire. Silently, it mobilizes the supreme spirits and subtly dissolves demonic obstructions. Those who uphold it without cease will enjoy boundless blessings and fortune.

*The Supreme Zhengyi Register of the Golden Bridge for Deliverance and Transformation* (1 grade).
This register crosses the stellar fords, repels celestial dogs, ascends the rainbow bridge without hindrance, and seizes propitious dreams to open the way. It eternally safeguards descendants and perpetuates familial blessings.

*The Supreme Register for Extending Life, Preserving Destiny, and Protecting the Body* (1 grade).
This register preserves destiny through the Three Primes, conceals the form within the Five Dippers, delivers from calamity, supports the frail, stabilizes the spirit, and extends lifespan. Those who receive and wear it with utmost sincerity will enjoy abundant blessings and fortune.

*The Supreme Zhengyi Register of Talismans for Resolving Karmic Punishments and the Six Harmful Influences* (1 grade).
This register resolves karmic punishments and harmful influences in one’s destiny, averts widowhood, solitary stars, and orphaned hours, harmonizes husband and wife, and extends lifespan.

*The Supreme Register for Reversing and Resolving the Five Tones’ Curses* (1 grade).
This register dissolves the causes of grievances, halts and removes curses. Enmity melts like ice, and blessings flow like rivers.

*The Supreme Zhengyi Register of the Child General for Protecting the Body* (1 grade).
This register secures the body, preserves destiny, severs malevolent influences, and expels evil. It guards children and opens the path to wisdom.

*The Supreme Zhengyi Secret Articles for Examining and Summoning the Three Primes* (1 grade).

This register gathers and coils auspicious qi, summons the host of perfected beings, delivers from calamity, rescues from peril, severs evil, and repels wickedness. Those who diligently cultivate and uphold it will perpetually propagate its flourishing.

*The Supreme Register of the Northern Thearch’s Divine Incantations for Subduing Demons and Slaying Ghosts* (1 grade).
This register governs the myriad demons, commands divine officials, extends its influence to the eight extremities, and severs the ten thousand evils. Those who wear it with devoted sincerity will defend orthodoxy and eliminate demonic influences.

*The Supreme Register of the Cavern Abyss Samādhi Divine Incantations* (1 grade).
When epidemics and poisons spread, demonic qi infects, and deaths follow one after another without remedy, one should receive this register. The five pestilences will retreat afar, and lasting peace and prosperity will be preserved.

*The Supreme Cavern Mystery Numinous Treasure Register of the Nine Wondrous Precepts for Cultivating Perfection in Advance* (1 grade).
This register’s principles derive from the Cavern Mystery and are expounded in the Numinous Treasure scriptures. Those who awaken to the Nine Precepts transcend the mundane and enter sageliness; those who wear its two talismans escape suffering and ascend to perfection. When the time comes for karmic dissolution, those who have cultivated in advance while alive will witness this register’s boundless blessings, eternally sustaining both humans and heavens.

*The Supreme Cavern Mystery Numinous Treasure Golden Record Register for Delivering Destiny, Rebirth, and Receiving the Ten Palaces’ and Five Marchmounts’ Yellow Register for Pre-Cultivation* (1 set, totaling 22 grades).
This register solemnly proclaims the wondrous canon and assigns its administration to the true bureaus. If transmitted on this day, one avoids the fault of repeated disrespect. In the future, its verification will yield the merit of delivering beings tenfold.

In this life, it augments fortune and longevity; on another day, it spreads bridges for passage. With utmost sincerity and faith, one receives boundless wondrous benefits.

*The Supreme Cavern Mystery Numinous Treasure Golden Register for Delivering Destiny and the Ten Palaces of the Netherworld and the Eastern Marchmount to Rescue Departed Souls* (1 set, totaling 22 grades).
This register washes away transgressions, absolves sins, saves the suffering, and delivers the departed. Who lacks a heart of filial piety? One must rely on the scriptures of posthumous cultivation. By submitting secret petitions on their behalf and presenting them to the netherworld bureaus, the departed are instantly illumined by returning light, enabling them to ascend to perfection and receive deliverance. With a single heart of filial devotion, nine generations of ancestors ascend as immortals.

They reveal the Three Luminaries, harmonize the hundred spirits, ingest the yellow blossoms, and expand or contract primordial qi. Jade fields bloom with flowers, and one roams the Three Isles. Amid misty clouds and golden crucibles, the elixir is perfected, and one whistles in transcendence. The sun and moon of the Nine Empyreans are attained; emptiness is embraced, and the One is held. One strides through the void and ascends the heavens. Those who receive and practice these registers have their names inscribed in the immortal rosters, advance in rank within the celestial palaces, and enable nine generations of ancestors to transcend and ascend.
