This register contains the Jade Clarity’s edicts of absolution, administered by the Three Officials. Those who wear it are protected by numinous officials and celestial soldiers. Any impending celestial punishments or netherworld retributions are absolved by its grace, rendering all pure and unblemished. If submitted on behalf of the departed through burning and presentation, they immediately attain transcendence and ascension.

*The Numinous Treasure Ascending Mystery Delivering and Saving Blood Lake Preserving Life True Register* (1 set);
*The Numinous Treasure Ascending Mystery Delivering and Saving Blood Lake Rescuing the Departed True Register* (1 set).
These registers were transmitted by the Primordial Beginning and decreed by the Primordial Sovereign. The earth harbors the prison of the Blood Lake, renowned in scriptures as the "Stone of Shame." All women in the world face the trials of childbirth; some bear the fruits of past-life evil, while others suffer present-life enmities. In pregnancy, they may harm the fetus, their pearls shattered like bees, their bodies departing the yang world, their souls cast into the yin pool. If devout women early awaken to benevolence and personally receive these precious registers—or if filial sons and obedient descendants do so on their behalf—their names are inscribed in the jade registers, their records erased from the dark bureaus. In their present lives, fortune and longevity increase; in the netherworld hereafter, they wander freely without hindrance. The merit of delivering the living and saving the dead is boundless.

*The Highest Divine Empyrean Jade Mansion Grand Commander-in-Chief Governing the Dragon-Tiger Mysterious Altar Golden Chariot Marshal Zhao Yuan Secret Register* (1 grade).
This register contains the mysterious mechanisms of the Jade Mansion and the secret canon of the Golden Chariot. Since the Patriarch refined the elixir at Dragon-Tiger, the Marshal has presided over the Mysterious Altar. The Eight Kings correspond to the spirits of the Eight Trigrams, and the Five Tigers display the valor of the Five Directions. They summon clouds and bring rain, dispel plagues and expel evil. Those who revere and uphold this register protect themselves and bring peace to their families; those who embody and practice it benefit others and all things.

Having revered the incense and flame, one should wear the sacred writ.

*The Supreme Orthodox Unity Zhao Marquis Secret Register for Expelling Evil and Averting Pestilence through the Correct Orifices*, one section.
This register contains the sacred writ of the correct orifices and the true forms of the precious talismans. The seventy-two seasonal toxins dissolve without command; the twenty-four black demons flee at the mere scent of the wind. It prolongs life and preserves destiny, guards the upright and expels evil—its divine transformations are boundless. It is fitting to wear and receive.

*The Supreme Nine Heavens Mysterious Woman Secret Register for Beheading Evil*, one grade.
This register reverently executes the celestial statutes and commands the thunder soldiers. Should any spectral evil in the lower realm—whether from the northern Yin or the Wu-You hours—emerge from caves, coil in mountains and forests, or spy upon households to harm lives, wherever the divine might reaches, all shall be swept away. It blesses the living, purges demonic influences, and responds without limit to those who wear it with sincerity.

*The Supreme Great Cavern Nine Heavens Transformative Wenchang Controller of Destiny Purple Yang Treasure Register*, one section.
This register holds the profound decrees of the Nine Heavens and the numinous chapters of the Seven Bends. Concealed within the Purple Yang’s cloud-brocade pouch, it was inscribed by the Heavenly Perfected Sovereign. It expansively unfolds the mysteries of the Dao and further illuminates the Confucian ethos. Those who wear it find their minds enlightened; those who comprehend it attain sudden clarity of their innate nature. Their names are inscribed in the cassia registers, their paths in the thorny enclosures aided by spirits. Scholars of literature, devote yourselves to its transmission.

*The Supreme Cavern Mystery Numinous Treasure Golden Register Scripture for Delivering Lives from the Ten Palaces of the Netherworld and the Eastern Marchmount’s Salvation of the Departed Souls*, one section in twenty-two fascicles.
*The Supreme Cavern Mystery Numinous Treasure Nine Perfected Wondrous Precepts Golden Register Scripture for Delivering Lives*, one section.
*The Supreme Numinous Treasure Scripture for Delivering from the Blood Lake*, one section.
*The Supreme Northern Dipper Original Destiny Longevity True Scripture*, one section.
*The Supreme Three-Five Capital Twenty-Four Treatises Scripture of the Libationers*, one section.

The above true scriptures are inscribed on cinnabar terraces and jade tablets, celestial writings in cloud-seal script, proclaimed by the Most High and received by the Heavenly Master. The scriptures form the essence, while the registers constitute their application. They may exist in relation to one another but cannot be without each other. Having studied the registers of the Daoist methods, further wear the true scriptures—essence and application share a single source, benefiting both self and others.

*Attending Perfected Plain Women*, *orthodox fifth rank*.
*Upper Wisdom Wondrous Immortal Women*, *congruent fourth rank*.
*Upper Mystery Immortal Women*, *orthodox fourth rank*.
*Upper Clarity Inner Institute Incense-Holding Jade Women*.
*Attending Incense Jade Women*, knowing the affairs of the Purple Tenuity Inner Palace.
*Jade Perfected of the Rotating Mechanism Dipper Treasury Keepers of the Registers*, jointly knowing the affairs of the Purple Tenuity Inner Palace.

Formerly, when the Heavenly Master received the registers, female perfected ones were given the titles of Heavenly Consorts and Heavenly Concubines. Now, those who receive the registers dare not presume to use such titles, and only employ the term "female." However, they are prohibited from using or being promoted to titles involving "consort" or "concubine."

1. In the initial rank, if one saves and delivers ten or more persons within a year, one is promoted from Right Judge to Right Grand Judge. After another year, if one saves and delivers ten more persons, one is promoted to Left Judge. After saving and delivering ten or more additional persons, one is promoted to Left Grand Judge. After another year, if one saves and delivers twenty or more persons, one is promoted to the eighth rank. After another year, if one saves and delivers twenty or more persons, one is promoted to the seventh rank. After another year, if one saves and delivers twenty or more persons, one is promoted to the sixth rank. After two more years, if one saves and delivers thirty or more persons, one is promoted to the fifth rank. After two more years, if one saves and delivers one hundred or more persons, one is promoted to the fourth rank. After three more years, if one saves and delivers one hundred twenty or more persons, one is promoted to the third rank. After five more years, if one accumulates twelve merits, one is promoted to the second rank. After ten more years, if one accumulates one hundred twenty merits, one is promoted to the first rank. From the third rank upward, these are the highest ranks, and they cannot be lightly conferred. Only those with lofty merits and renowned conduct, whose names are recorded in the immortal registers, may attain them; such ranks cannot be described by mere grade.

2. Within the aforementioned years, if one’s merits in a given year are abundant, one may be promoted twice in that year, but one may not exceed two ranks in a single promotion.

If one’s merits are abundant but one does not wish to accept promotion, one may instead be reassigned to serve as a general or officer.

1. If within a year one has neither merits nor faults, one shall remain in one’s current position as before.

2. If within a year one has both merits and faults, these may only offset one another.

3. If one idly wastes time, accumulating faults without merits, and lacks the conduct of a general or officer, how can one privately evade self-indictment and scrutiny? Such a person ought to indict themselves—how could they presume to advance?

4. Saving lives is called *merit*; accumulating virtue is called *conduct*. What is termed *one merit* is roughly equivalent to saving one hundred persons. Calculated by fractions: saving ten or more persons may be counted as one-tenth of a merit. Extending the nation’s lifespan or resolving great crises—matters concerning salvation and relief—count as two merits. Praying for clear skies or rain on behalf of the people, driving away locusts, alleviating plagues, or averting floods and fires to benefit the people and all living things counts as one merit. If malevolent spirits or entangled curses manifest visibly and are widely resented, and one eradicates their root, this counts as one merit. For other cases involving one-tenth of a merit or more, the weight is assessed and converted accordingly. Performing rituals to eliminate misfortune or invoke blessings, completing jiao offerings, refining souls to resolve grievances, petitioning for the people’s lives, or achieving clear karmic retribution with verifiable benefits to salvation counts as one merit. For other cases, the weight is assessed and converted accordingly. Saving a woman in difficult childbirth, ensuring the survival of both mother and child, counts as one merit. If either mother or child is lost, this is calculated from one-tenth of a merit upward. Matters not fully enumerated here are to be assessed and converted according to reason.

5. Concurrently serving in the Central Heaven Court, Supreme Ultimate Court, Demon-Quelling Court, Yellow Register Court, Supreme Clarity Court, Purple Court, and Southern Palace, as well as the Refinement-Receiving Bureau and other courts:
   - From the ninth to the seventh rank, one is titled *Concurrently Supervising Affairs of [Court Name]*.
   - From the sixth to the fourth rank, one is titled *Concurrently Overseeing Affairs of [Court Name]*.
   - From the third to the second rank, one is titled *Concurrently Directing Affairs of [Court Name]*.
   - Those of the ninth rank and above concurrently serve as Refinement-Receiving Officers of the Southern Palace.
   - Those of the fifth rank and above concurrently serve as Directors of the Yellow Register Court.
   - From the ninth to the seventh rank, one additionally holds the office of *Commanding the Affairs of the Three Realms’ Spirits and Demons*.
   - From the eighth to the seventh rank, one additionally holds the office of *Overseeing the Affairs of the Three Realms’ Spirits and Demons*.
   - From the seventh rank upward, one additionally holds the office of *Overseeing the City God Bureau*.
   - From the sixth rank upward, one additionally holds the office of *Overseeing the City God Bureaus of the Nine Provinces*.
   - At the fifth rank, one additionally holds the office of *Commanding the Soldiers and Horses of the Sacred Mountains’ City Gods*.
   - At the fourth rank, one additionally holds the office of *Commander-in-Chief of the Soldiers and Horses of the Sacred Mountains and Rivers*.
   - At the third rank, one additionally holds the office of *Commanding the Soldiers and Horses of the Nine Heavens*.
   - At the second rank, one additionally holds the office of *Investigating the Spirits and Demons of the Three Realms and Adjudicating the Affairs of Grotto-Heavens, Blessed Lands, and Purification Halls*.

6. When a beginning adept receives Daoist methods, they must first receive the register, allowing them to be appointed to the rank of adjunct ninth rank. Those who have not received the register may not be appointed to the regular ninth rank.

7. In performing zhai and jiao rituals, even if one holds another rank, if one has not received the register and lacks the *Dugong* register or the position of *Jijiu*, one’s sincerity will not reach the gods. Those of the seventh rank and above who have not received the *Mengwei* register may not be appointed. Those of the fifth rank and above who have not received the *Dongyuan* register may not be appointed. Those of the fourth rank and above who have not received the *Shenxiao* register may not be appointed. Those of the third rank and above who have not received the *Great Cavern* register may not be appointed.

8. Methods and registers are mutually dependent and must not conflict. The *Tianxin* method is suited to the *Dugong* register. The *Five Thunders* method is suited to the *Highest Divine Empyrean* register. The *Lingbao* method is suited to the *Purple Void Yang Light* register and the *Lingbao Middle Alliance* register. The *Tianpeng* method is suited to the *Northern Emperor Demon-Quelling* register. The *Tianshu* method is suited to the *Highest Clarity Returning Chariot and Dipper* register. The *Zhao Hou Southern* method has its own proper register, suited to the *Zhao Hou* register.

9. The *Tianxin* method is the ancestor of all methods. The *Dugong* and *Mengwei* registers encompass twenty-four ranks and should be received first.

10. The Southern and Northern Courts are called the *civil ranks*, while the Thunder Bureau is called the *military ranks*. For beginning adepts, it is easier to enter the military ranks from the civil ranks, but difficult to enter the civil ranks from the military ranks.

11. The *Five Thunders* are:
    - *Heavenly Thunder*, the bureau of the heavens’ attendants;
    - *Divine Thunder*, the command center of thunder and lightning;
    - *Dragon Thunder*, the guardian of the sea’s treasuries;
    - *Water Thunder*, the bureau governing rain and moisture;
    - *Community Thunder*, the spirits of famous mountains and great rivers who receive blood sacrifices through loyalty.
    These serve the Emperor above and attend to the people’s affairs below, and may be commanded accordingly.

12. The *Four Bureaus* are:
    Within the Jade Treasury’s Five Thunders Envoys’ Court, there is the *True Lord of the Jade Treasury’s Five Thunders Envoys’ Court*, who presides over thunder and specifically governs the *Jade Pivot Five Thunders Court*. Additionally, there is the *Thunder Bureau*, which administers punishments, and the *Penglai Water Bureau*, which governs water and moisture. These three bureaus are all under the jurisdiction of the *Jade Treasury’s Five Thunders Envoys’ Court*. All cases of exoneration and imprisonment must not be presumptuously handled by the Pivot Bureau but are instead sent to the *Thunder Bureau*. The quota of the *Five Thunders Envoys’ Court* must not be arbitrarily used.

13. When a beginning adept receives methods, they must seek a master of the current generation who is pure in conduct and upright in learning, and pay homage to them. The master, too, should select disciples of true capacity and only then transmit the teachings. First, one must summon guarantor officials and guarantor allies, present a sincere petition, and obtain clear guarantees before proceeding according to the proper forms. Memorials are submitted, and upon approval, one is ordained and granted the *Divine Empyrean Illumination Certificate*, the *Title Deed*, and other documents. Next, a jiao ritual is held to thank the master, and the methods are received and brought back to the altar.

14. If within a year one has merits warranting promotion according to seniority, one must summon fellow method officials of the same rank to provide guarantees, submit a petition to the ordination master as before, and memorialize for approval and transmission. This must not be treated with negligence or irreverence. If the master is not of upright learning and the disciple is hasty and reckless, their names may not be recorded in the immortal registers, and the heavens will not attend to them. Only wayward shrines and lesser ghosts will falsely claim their names, inviting disasters. The true bureaus will investigate, and the resulting offenses will not be light.

15. When a beginning adept receives methods and accumulates merits leading to promotion, they must still report to their master for transmission. They must provide a detailed account of the beginning and end of their progress, including the year and month, the names of their master and guarantors, the methods they practice, the merits they have accumulated, and the rank to which they are to be promoted. A petition is submitted to the *Celestial Master of Orthodox Unity at the Mysterious Altar*, who memorializes and issues the certificate. Only then will their name be recorded in the Jade Registers, and gods and humans will revere them. If one presumptuously exaggerates their merits, boasts to the world, or fails to report to a master and instead fraudulently fabricates ranks, falsely claiming promotions, or if one receives methods without proper transmission from a master and recklessly writes down official ranks, treating them as empty formalities, this will mislead the Mysterious Altar. What efficacy could there be in memorializing and issuing certificates under such circumstances?

Discipline is clear as daylight—heed it! Be vigilant!

**Chapter on Revolving Creation and Transformation**
**The Three-Five Flying Steps and Ranks of the Dang**

The Master said: The secrets of the Three-Five—how could they be easily known? From One, Two arises; from Two, Three is born. For the Three Qi divide and the Three Lights shine; the Three Lights shine and the Three Powers are complete.

From the Great Ultimate, the Two Modes emerge; from the Two Modes, the Four Images arise. When the Four Images are complete, the Five Phases are whole; when the Five Phases are whole, the Five Stars shine; when the Five Stars shine, the Five Peaks stand firm. Thus, in the Dao they become the Three Pure Ones; in the world, the Three Powers; among spirits, the Three Origins; in humans, they correspond to the Three Sections. Again, in the Dao they are the Five Elders; in Heaven, the Five Stars; on Earth, the Five Peaks; in humans, the Five Viscera.

Humans possess Heaven and Earth, their forms divided into yin and yang. The Dao of qi is complete within the body, yet if one cannot nurture the Three Fields to gestate refinement or allow the Five Viscera to receive the numinous, then one begins to drift far from the Dao.

Those who cultivate it gather treasures in the Three Fields and summon the Five Qi to return to the Origin. The po is restrained, the hun is bound, spirit is whole, and qi is full—this is the immortal’s Way of prizing life. Those who do not cultivate it allow the Three Hun to become the Three Corpses, the Five Qi to become the Five Thieves, and the Five Thieves to become the Five Sufferings—this is the ghostly Way of prizing death.

Thus, among all things between Heaven and Earth, humans are the most numinous. Therefore, every gesture of hand and step of foot is none other than an alignment with the Real. The method of stepping the Dang arises from this.

The stepping of the Dang is the essence of flying Heaven and the spirit of treading Earth, the true movement of humans. It causes the Three Powers to unite in virtue and the Nine Qi to merge as one. All ghosts and spirits revolve with Heaven and Earth. Each step and point, each turn and revolution, is complete within the workings of creation. The numinous is at one’s left.

Thus, one step resembles the Great Ultimate; two steps, the Two Modes; three steps, the Three Powers; four steps, the Four Seasons; five steps, the Five Phases; six steps, the Six Pitch Pipes; seven steps, the Seven Stars; eight steps, the Eight Trigrams; nine steps, the Nine Numinous Ones—this is the origin of the ten thousand steps.

The Master said: The method of the Yu Step has lost its authenticity in the world. Though many can speak of it, few truly attain it. Even those who attain it do not practice it, and those who practice it do so without devotion—thus, its efficacy is rarely manifest.

The Huoluo Dipper practiced in the world today is the pivotal essence of the Three-Five Yu Step, the comprehensive number of the intersecting River Chart. How could it be dismissed as ordinary? Yet due to errors in transmission, it cannot transform or communicate with the numinous. I now correct these errors to transmit its true form.

The Master said: One Qi divides into Three, named Mysterious, Origin, and Beginning. When the Three Qi divide, the Three Powers are established. The human body mirrors this: the pure and turbid form is divided into Three Sections, each with its own spirit—also called the Three Fields. Each field holds its treasure. Thus, from One comes Two, from Two comes Three—this is the true within our bodies. Together, they are called the Three Origins.

*Origin* means greatness, primacy. Thus, the *Qian* hexagram in the *Book of Changes* calls the Origin "the chief of goodness."

The Master said: The spirits of the Two and Five penetrate Heaven and Earth, yet all return to the single body. In their operation, there are methods of generation, conquest, restraint, and submission. When petitioning or offering thanks, one employs the generative cycle; when restraining or driving away, one employs the conquest cycle.

Whenever stepping the Dang, first summon the spirits of the Three Origins and Five Phases, then proceed with the steps.

The Master said: The ancestral qi of the Five Phases is called the Five Elders. *Elder* means origin, ancestor. Drawing the essence of the Five Elders forms the Five Stars; the flowing essence of the Five Stars congeals to form the Five Peaks. Matched to the human body, they are called the Five Viscera. Above, they correspond to the Five Stars; in the center, to the Five Peaks—thus, the spirits reside within them.

The Five Phases and Five Virtues generate one another: Wood generates Fire. The Five Phases and Five Qi conquer one another: Metal conquers Wood.

**Upper Origin Dang (Attributed to Heaven)**
*Incantation for Stepping the Upper Origin Dang:*
Step the essence of Heaven, command the ten thousand spirits.
The Upper Origin shields my body.
General Tanghong, assist my true qi,
repel and subdue demonic spirits.
Whoever dares harm me,
let them suffer in their own person.
May evil demons, upon seeing me,
be reduced to fine dust.
*Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by law!*

**Middle Origin Dang (Attributed to Humans)**
*Incantation for Stepping the Middle Origin Dang:*
Step the essence of humans, strengthen yang to disperse yin.
Fortify my Three Hun,
exterminate ghosts and banish essences.
Misfortune cannot reach me,
calamity cannot invade.
The Middle Origin conceals my form.
General Geyong, lead a thousand, ten thousand troops
to guard my body.
*Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by law!*

**Lower Origin Dang (Attributed to Earth)**
*Incantation for Stepping the Lower Origin Dang:*
Tread the spirit of Earth, secure the human Dao.
Heaven revolves, Earth turns,
above, the *Kui*; below, the *Qian*.
Yin closes, yang opens,
true qi flows ceaselessly.
Ghosts cannot harm me,
humans cannot injure me.
Heaven is my canopy,
Earth is my support.
Whoever dares harm me,
be pressed and sent to the *Kui* Dang.
The Lower Origin hides my form.
General Zhouwu, follow wherever I go,
hasten to protect this true one.
*Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by law!*

The Master said: When restraining fierce evil or overcoming disasters and dangers, first step the Upper Origin Dang. After completing the sequence in order, enter the Middle Origin Dang, then transform into the Lower Origin Dang. If restraining fierce evil, further transform into the Five Phases Conquest Dang to subdue Heavenly Dragons and ghosts. Spirits will respond to the heart’s summons—nothing will fail. Guard this secret!

**Five Phases Conquest Dang**
The Master said: When restraining fierce evil or overcoming disasters and dangers, step this Dang. For example, Water can conquer Fire—thus, one applies the method as needed. To restrain fire calamities, step Metal and Water to control Fire. The rest follow this pattern. If later students are unclear, simply complete the stepping of the Dang without additions or omissions.

*Incantation:*
The Five Phases mutually destroy:
Earth and Water sever each other;
Water and Fire extinguish each other;
Metal and Wood assault each other.
May ghosts and demons, upon seeing me—?

"Sever the head, sever the feet.
The Demon Kings tremble in fear, torn asunder above and below.
Whoever dares to transgress shall forever sink into the dark abyss—
Swiftly, swiftly, as the law commands!"

This Dang follows the pattern of Metal conquering Wood, Wood conquering Earth, Earth conquering Water, Water conquering Fire, and Fire conquering Metal. It is employed for restraining and subduing.

**Five Phases Mutual Generation Dang**
The Master of Wood said: The Mutual Generation Dang follows Wood generating Fire. One generates, one destroys—all proceed according to the reckoning of Water as one, Fire as two, Wood as three, Metal as four, and Earth as five, completing fifteen steps in the three-and-five Dao.

*Incantation:*
The Five Phases mutually generate—
All affairs prosper and flourish.
Water and Wood achieve perfection,
Fire and Earth unite in harmony,
Metal and Wood advance together.
Calamity transforms into fortune,
Ghosts cannot harm,
People cannot encroach.
The dead revive,
The withered flourish anew—
Swiftly, swiftly, as the law commands!

**Yu’s Steps of the Ninefold Numinous Dipper Dang**
Sun and Moon shine bright,
Heaven and Earth pair in union.
I enter the Dipper from Tianpeng,
Pass lightly by Tianchong, meet Fu, then retreat,
Return to Tianqin, facing the heart.
Embrace the Pillar of Heaven, freely gathering with the heroic,
The Dipper’s Dao flows—ghostly paths crumble—
Swiftly, swiftly, as the law commands!

The Master said: *Huoluo* is the Dipper. This is called the Lesser Three-and-Five Dang. The world often remains unaware of its details, taking habitual practice for granted, ignorant of its profound subtleties. This Dang can subdue wild evil, command ghosts and spirits, and dismantle temples—its applications are many. When reversed in use, errors arise; now, the correct method is restored.

Essential and wondrous, the Dipper governs the twelve celestial hours,
Riding radiant light, martial might arrays.
Qi drifts like floating clouds,
The Seven Stars transform, corresponding to Heaven above.
Know their transformations—fortune and misfortune arise.
Enter the celestial lodges, cross the Heavenly Gate,
Align with the Six Pitches, grasp the cyclical stems.
Tread upon Tianying, mount Tianren,
Plunge into the limpid abyss—yet walk upon land,
Lean upon the Pillar of Heaven, embrace the Heart of Heaven.
From here, ascend to Tianqin,
Rely on Tianfu, gaze toward Tianchong,
Enter the Dipper’s depths, emerge from Tianpeng.
The Dipper’s Dao flows—hard and soft harmonize,
Augmenting fortune and emolument, leaving blessings for posterity.
Emerge from darkness—live a thousand myriad years,
A thousand ghosts, ten thousand spirits naturally retreat—
Swiftly, swiftly, as the law commands!

The Master said: This Dang, as commonly practiced, enters and exits the Dipper in reverse, hence its inefficacy. Now, the correct method is established—thus may one command ghosts and spirits, expel demonic paths.
Guard this secret! Guard this secret!

The **Golden Light Encompassing Dang**

The Master said: Whenever ascending the altar to perform rituals, visualize yourself as the Divine Yu. Recite the incantation while forming the mudra, beginning with the *Jade Script* and ending with the *Noon Script*. Tread the Dang, traversing all within Heaven and Earth. Golden light encircles your body, transforming your form to subdue demons. Utter the sounds of *tiyin* and *zhali*. Envision before you a sphere of purple *qi*; soon, green *qi* descends from Heaven, piercing the purple *qi*. Suddenly, amidst the clouds, golden palaces and towering pavilions appear. Bow thrice in reverence, offering obeisance, and present your petition according to ritual.

When treading this Dang, recite the *Golden Light Incantation*, one step for each phrase. Upon completing the incantation, proceed with the Dipper Dang.

**The Yu King’s Three Steps and Nine Traces**
The Master said: Visualize yourself standing atop Yu’s Dragon Gate excavation, amidst wind, thunder, and cloud *qi*, bearing the Mandate of the Supreme Emperor. With the left hand forming the Jade Mudra and the right wielding the Sword Mudra, summon and dispatch the myriad spirits as the matter requires.

**The Mudra Technique**
The Master said: Mudras serve to commune with the true and subdue the perverse. Each mudra differs; the Dang mudras number over seven hundred, though few are now in use. The four cardinal directions and eight trigrams are marked by counting the joints of the four fingers, totaling twelve points corresponding to the twelve earthly branches. Within these, the Eight Trigrams, Seven Stars, Nine Palaces, and Three Terraces each govern their respective affairs. To simplify: the central joint of the middle finger is the *Jade Clarity Mudra*, while its left side is the *Northern Emperor Mudra*, known as the *Great Slaying Script*. These two mudras govern all matters across the Three Realms—employ them accordingly.

**The Teeth-Tapping Technique**
The Master said: Tapping the teeth gathers the true and assembles the spirits. When a person’s *qi* scatters and the heart’s *qi* dissipates, true *qi* fails to respond—thus it must be gathered.

Tapping the teeth stirs the Gate of Heaven, summoning the spirit-*qi*. The left tap sounds the *Heavenly Bell*, the right the *Heavenly Chime*. For subduing, driving away, or descending spirits, use the front teeth—four above and four below, eight in total—tapping them together to sound the *Dharma Drum*, thereby communing with the true and reaching the Supreme Emperor. For audience petitions, tap thrice above and below, totaling twenty-four strikes, known as sounding the *Dharma Drum*. Remember this always.

**The Entering the Chamber Technique**
The Master said: When establishing an altar, the chamber’s entrance lies in the southeast, the *Xun* earthly gate. If entering during a *jing* ritual, treat the *jing* gate as the entrance. Step through here, first tapping the teeth twelve times at *Xun*, bowing thrice in the heart, then advancing the right foot followed by the left. First visualize the Four Attendant Heralds and the Two Dragon-Tiger Lords standing to your left and right. Next, envision the chamber filled with blue, yellow, and white clouds of *qi*, then see the incense smoke form five colors, rising straight to the Golden Gates. Bow nine times—or simply in the heart, if preferred.

**The Incense-Burning Technique**
The Master said: Enter the chamber with the left foot first, never glancing back—lest you invite misfortune. Maintain a single-minded stillness. Visualize the Azure Dragon to your left, the White Tiger to your right, the Vermilion Bird before you, and the Dark Warrior behind. The Heralds and Jade Maidens ride the five-colored *qi* of your five viscera, ascending straight to the Three Heavens. Focus your thoughts without obstruction. When you feel a gentle warmth within, it is the true *qi* uniting with virtue.

When burning incense, ensure a blazing fire. Then, pinch the incense and place it in the censer—this is called *offering incense*. *Feng* means abundance; let the smoke rise in a single, vigorous ascent, reaching without delay. If the incense smoke frays or the flame weakens, it cannot transcend to the true or reach the numinous.

Always hold the incense in the left hand—the *rubbing hand*. The right hand is impure and must not touch the incense.

**The Incense-Petition Technique**
The Master said: Maintain a heart free of external distractions and inner杂念. See only true light and Brahman *qi* before you, with purple and azure *qi* filling the space ahead and behind. Cast aside all thoughts, ascending directly to the Ten Directions. Offer incense to the Ten Directions, and true *qi* descends to meet the incense smoke within the *qi*. Vaguely perceive the boundless true immortals and celestial lords arriving from all directions amidst fine rain and dense mist. Then, at the ritual table, see the incense transform into five colors. The Heralds and Talisman Clerks appear in the void. Your body seems to ascend to the Three Heavens, where you personally behold the Three Pure Ones and the Jade Emperor. Tap your teeth thirty-six times, swallow the saliva nine times, then proceed according to the ritual.

The Master said: Beginners in the Dao are prone to wandering thoughts and doubts; do not burden them with elaborate texts. Within simplicity, observe and contemplate—the subtlety lies beyond words. If one can advance in rank and ascend the mystery, from here to inheriting the lineage, attaining immortality is not difficult.

**The Petition-Presenting Technique**
The Master said: When presenting petitions, healing illnesses, or deploying talismans, first visualize the Primordial Beginning in the Upper Cinnabar Field, the Dao Lord in the Middle Cinnabar Field, and the Old Lord in the Lower Cinnabar Field. Then visualize the Three Palaces and Three Perfected Ones, each in your likeness. First, envision the Lord within the Lower Cinnabar Field merging with the Dao Lord in your heart, standing together in your crown as if seated in a golden palace. Your body kneels in obeisance as you secretly present your petition—immediate resonance will follow.

**The Audience with the True and Emperor-Visiting Technique**
The Master said: A humble novice is but an ordinary person, with desires for food, drink, and sensuality no different from others. Yet now, having received the registers and practiced the methods, you are called a Dharma Master, donning starry crowns and cloud-patterned robes, aspiring to resemble immortals and sages. But if your heart remains unsettled, your *qi* restless, still entangled in lust and impurity, tainted by filth and stench—how can you hope to visit the Supreme Emperor beyond the void? Without the method of clarity and brightness, you cannot evoke resonance but will instead incur transgressions.

Thus it is said: Even an evil person, through purification, fasting, and bathing, may serve the Supreme Emperor. This is the meaning.

**The Fasting and Offering Audience Technique**
The Master said: During offerings and audience rituals, adhere to the prescribed forms, merging body and mind. Constantly visualize the Golden Gates high above the vault of Heaven, unaware of standing on the altar, sensing only that you are amidst the Nine Empyreans. In recitation and visualization, sever all delusive thoughts.

Thus does profound resonance arise—not merely in outward ritual.

**The Prayer and Petition Technique**
The Master said: In ordinary times, frequently examine yourself. Enter stillness, sit in silence, and cast aside all mundane concerns. When your *qi* and bearing settle, envision within the empty vastness atop your crown a jade hall with golden towers, where the Heavenly Worthy sits in golden majesty. Sustain this visualization until you feel the true *qi* suffusing your fontanel, a subtle warmth radiating inward. This is the method for daily practice.

When matters arise, employ the same visualization and align your body, suddenly finding yourself kneeling before the Heavenly Worthy. Silently offer your prayers, and nothing will fail to be answered. These are the essential instructions of the lineage masters, passed down to guide disciples in their first steps. This is the wondrous technique for ascending the hall and entering the inner chamber—guard it well, and do not reveal it to the uninitiated.

**The Talisman-Writing Technique**
The Master said: In writing talismans, the key is to settle the mind and exclude all external thoughts. The brushstrokes must be precise yet fluid, so that when you begin, spirit does not wander nor *qi* scatter. If you recite the text while writing, the talisman may take form, but if your eyes shift, intent follows, and the mind strays with the brush, resonance will not arise.

The mind must unite with the talisman, the talisman with the mind. Draw *qi* without hesitation, exhale it silently, and inscribe the talisman—this is called "self-transmitting the joyous spirit," for it speaks to the mind’s steadfast clarity. Later sections will elaborate in detail; beginners should first master this.

*Direct Pointers to the Jade Hall*

The Master said: The Jade Hall is the esoteric core of the Celestial Heart Ancestral Teachings, the wellspring from which all methods flow, the revered path of the Three Realms. Since the time of the Celestial Master of Han, it has been transmitted solely as a mind-seal, devoid of extraneous techniques—nothing but orthodoxy. Orthodoxy means the absence of deviation. Heaven covers and nurtures through orthodoxy; Earth bears and sustains through orthodoxy; *qi* circulates through orthodoxy; ghosts and spirits are commanded through orthodoxy. When a person rectifies the heart, the body follows; if the heart is not rectified, deviant thoughts arise, the Six Desires stir, and one degenerates into a beast or sinks into the realm of hungry ghosts. Those who, in this world, fail to uphold orthodoxy become treacherous and perverse, rebelling against the Dao, and are barred from the domain of true immortals. The emergence of the great teachings of the Jade Hall originates with the Orthodox Celestial Master. Orthodoxy precludes deviation; unity precludes duality.

Those who inherit this teaching are divided into five ranks. For those in the world who weary of dust and aspire to truth, upon first entering the altar, they receive the *Ten Scrolls of the Orthodox Celestial Heart Method*. After practicing for three years, free from disrespect toward the master or contempt for the Dao, and without slackening in diligence, they may proceed to the next stage, receiving the seventh rank. If their conduct remains faultless, they advance two ranks, don the seal of the Jade Altar’s orthodox rank, and are permitted to ascend the High Flight to the Jade Capital. After twelve years of practice, if proven not to be among the common rabble of markets and streets, nor of the ranks of servants, menials, corrupt clerks, or oppressive officials, and if not merely dull-witted parasites in temples and abbeys, they may be entrusted with the supreme宗旨, the *Twenty-Four Ranks*, the *Three Ascents Precious Registers*, and the seals of the *Three Sceneries of the Jade Hall*. The *Jade Scenery Ascending the Hall Seal* designates them as lineage-holding branch masters. "Branch" signifies the division into separate streams. This transmission is not limited in number but is restricted to gentlemen of official rank, scholars of Confucian or Mohist refinement—all may bear and uphold it. It is forbidden to transmit it to the common Daoist clergy of the marketplace.

In this age, many among the Daoist clergy are those who, destitute and forsaken, rejected by the four classes of society, turn to donning the yellow cap and entering the Dao not out of sincere devotion but out of desperation. Such individuals may treat the sacred texts with disdain, lose the secret teachings, and incur unforgivable transgressions. The above describes the fourth rank. Transmission and ordination.

For the fifth-rank transmission lineage, the lineage-holding master transmits solely to one rightful successor. They confer the Twenty-Four Forbidden Scriptures in jade script, the *Xuanhe Sword for Beheading Demons*, and the *Seal for Summoning Perfected Beings and Subduing Demons*. Only after thirty years may this transmission be passed on. Now, with the initial rank and first stage of ordination, its texts are concise, its practice simplified—every person may uphold it, and all may gaze in aspiration toward the Jade Hall.

On the day of ascending the altar, the disciple advances with measured steps, bearing the pledge of faith and oath. Even if one holds high office or noble rank, they must not slight the Perfected or disdain the Dao. They shall bow nine times before the altar of covenant to receive the transmission.

From this moment, they bear the mystery of the Dao and must not contravene the master’s instructions. Henceforth, they ascend the path of immortals and enter the gate of the Inaudible and Invisible. Should one fail to heed this teaching, transmitting recklessly or receiving lightly, the Three Officials shall record their transgressions, the Four Administrators shall tally their faults, and the Heavenly Bureau shall pronounce judgment. Their seven generations of ancestors shall suffer retribution in the trials of the Wind-Knife, their souls bound to eternal night. Ten thousand repentances cannot cleanse this, a thousand Perfected Ones cannot redeem it. Thus, transmission must be conducted with utmost care.

The practice of the initial rank’s teachings is transmitted orally and sealed in the heart, comprising twenty matters:

1. Each day, cultivate with reverence and diligence, gradually distancing oneself from worldly affairs. One must not mingle with the dust of the vulgar or engage in frivolous pursuits. Over time, as the precepts and conduct become radiant, one may proceed to the next stage of transmission.

2. Preserve and refine the *qi* of the Radiant Yang and Conjoined Yin. Devote oneself to its circulation, and in time, true *qi* will suffuse the body. Through exhalation and inhalation, one becomes Perfected, and without conscious effort, ghosts and spirits will stand in awe.

3. Upon receiving the teachings in full, take the Great Dao as the ancestral root. In all actions, maintain right mindfulness and never entertain wayward thoughts.

4. Each morning, recite the true scriptures and secret incantations. Rise early to offer incense, meditating in silence without vocalizing. Let the heart alone resonate, and never allow worldly affairs to disrupt this regular practice.

5. When encountering malevolent spirits or wicked demons harming the people, act strictly in accordance with orthodox teachings, ensuring their execution without fail. If one harbors fear or seeks favor from ghosts and spirits, this betrays a divided heart and incurs grave offense. The Three Officials shall punish without pardon or reprieve.

6. Employ celestial generals and officials with rightful intent. Never use blood offerings to mingle impure *qi*. Violators shall be penalized by the Three Officials.

7. Take the Three Luminaries as the foundation. The Three Luminaries are the eyes of Heaven and Earth, the root of yin and yang, and the ancestral origin of creation. Cultivate the heart and circulate true *qi*, merging with the Imperial Perfected Threefold Radiance as one. Not only will this subdue the Three Realms and bind demonic spirits, but one’s own body shall radiate light, all spirits shall stand in awe, corpses shall be repelled, illness expelled, and one shall attain the Dao and long life, ascending to join the Immortal Perfected.

8. By day, preserve the Three Luminaries and ingest *qi*. By night, preserve the Dipper, presenting it to the body so that self and spirit become one, spirit and *qi* intermingling. Only then may one be called a lineage-holding master.

9. First practice the method of *Three-Eights Atonement*. At each fortnightly solar term, dispatch the body’s celestial generals to offer memorials and engage in cultivation as prescribed. If this is practiced without cease, one shall become a person without fault and may then speak of inheriting the Mystery Teachings.

10. Each day, ingest the talisman of the Three Luminaries and await its response.

11. Abstain from lust and anger. Always respond to the world with kindness and compassion. Sacrifice for others, never attack the root or slander the master, nor envy the worthy or resent the capable. Do not speak with a forked tongue or engage in quarrels and strife. If one has harbored such duality, from this day forward, reform and cultivate virtue. Constantly maintain a single-minded focus: distance oneself from wealth and profit, abandon deceit and flattery, reduce carnal desires, uphold fasting and precepts, and discipline the heart.

12. When offering incense, visualize the five-colored *qi* emanating from the five viscera, coalescing into a floral canopy that ascends to the Empty Mystery. The Celestial Thearch, gazing from the void, shall witness it, and thus the offering shall surely reach its destination.

13. When writing talismans, enter seclusion and stabilize the mind. Dip the brush and compose the talisman, holding the breath and reciting the incantation silently. Clench the fists firmly, adopting an unyielding demeanor. The body must be upright, the heart correct; the heart serene, the spirit responsive.

14. Merge the One Perfected with the Dao. Detach from all external affairs. Do not let the heart be distracted by phenomena or generate covetous thoughts. Reflect on the impermanence of worldly matters; only the Dao endures. Abide in the One Perfected, and the Void shall respond to the One Spirit.

15. Upon entering or exiting, visualize the Heavenly Soldiers, Merit-Officials, and Jade Maidens arrayed to the left and right. Evil shall not dare encroach upon the upright, and even if *qi* stirs with private impulse, preserve the visualization as before.

16. On the ten auspicious days, *gengshen* and *jiazi*, the Three Origins and Three Assemblies, the new and full moons, the eight solar terms, and the five seasonal festivals, retire to a separate chamber to contemplate the Perfected. Always maintain reverence as if hosting honored guests—this is most sublime.

17. Do not inwardly harbor cunning or treacherous thoughts while outwardly displaying a gentle and kind demeanor. Do not covet what is not rightfully yours. Seek only what is justly obtained. Violators must reflect on their faults, reform, and atone. Repeated offenses are forbidden.

18. Serve parents with filial piety. Do not let wealth or poverty alter one’s devotion. Obey and attend to them with joy. To oppose the wishes of one’s kin is called unfiliality. Unfiliality is a grave offense, admitting no pardon.

19. When parents pass away, exert all effort in sincere contemplation and prayer to the Celestial Thearch, seeking their deliverance from the dark realms and ascent to the Heavenly Halls. If parents remain in the gloom of the netherworld, one’s own immortal attainments shall not be fulfilled.

20. Treat brothers, clan members, distant relatives, and in-laws with harmony and kindness. Do not take sides to provoke disputes or harbor resentment, thereby losing the bond of kinship. Violators shall not command the obedience of spirits across the Three Realms. Exercise caution in such matters.

Conduct oneself within the bounds of rules and standards. Should the heart ever stray, correct it promptly. Aspire to stand shoulder to shoulder with the sages and worthies. Do not belittle oneself or entertain reckless thoughts.

**Rites and Regulations for Offering Ceremonies**

**Chapter on Ritual Forms for Offerings**

**Taiyi Fast:** Performed by emperors to extend ritual homage and align with Heaven.

**Nine Heavens Fast** and **Golden Register Fast:** Established by the state to pray for the prolongation of imperial reign.

**Jade Record Fast:** Conducted to protect and bless the empresses and the six palaces.

**Great Yellow Register Fast:** All possess ranks and grades; one must consult established precedents and not act recklessly. Those conducted by scholar-officials and commoners may only be termed "offering rites."

**River Chart, Mysterious Numinosity, and other offerings:** Encompassing dozens of names, all are offerings. In antiquity, "offering" was another name for sacrifice. No rite surpasses the offering in summoning the Celestial Thearch and assembling the myriad spirits.

1. State-sponsored offerings follow three-day or seven-day rituals. According to the *Lingbao Scripture*’s fast methods, there are twenty-seven days of observance. Du Guangting’s *Offering Grades* lists seventy-two ranks, all employed by the state. As with the *Three Caverns*’ ritual forms, each has its fixed model.

2. When officials, commoners, scholar-officials, or common households conduct offering fasts, they should limit them to one day and night. Some extend them to three or seven days and nights, but this risks irreverence and may instead incur divine censure. Even high officials do not stay overnight in the homes of commoners; how much less would the Supreme Thearch, dwelling in the ninefold heavens, condescend to remain among mortals for three or seven days and nights without returning? Thus, the offering regulations are set: for a one-day offering, preparations begin in advance, and on the appointed day, the rite commences at dawn and concludes by deep night, thereby avoiding disrespect to the sacred. The ritual forms and grades are recorded in the *Jade Palace* and *Mysterious Model* manuals; one may consult them as needed.

3. For grand offerings held to open the altar, the finest locations are grotto-heavens, blessed lands, and Daoist abbeys. The altar must be properly oriented, facing south with its back to the north. If an abbey already has an altar but its orientation is skewed, one may set up the altar in another suitable space according to the prescribed form.

4. When conducting an offering, one must act within one’s means: the wealthy prepare fully, while the poor adapt as they can. Do not use ill-gotten wealth for offering supplies, nor haggle over prices, nor hastily prepare when resources suffice, nor force arrangements beyond one’s capacity—all such acts lack sincerity and fail to move the spirits. If the sponsor is a household of loyalty and filial piety, exerting utmost effort, and the master performs rites on their behalf—such as presenting dragon silks—all matters should be simplified. The requisite documents, offerings, and other elements will naturally resonate with the divine.

5. The visualization techniques and methods employed during offering rites are recorded in the *Chapter on Circulating the Transformations of Qi*. The musical instruments and celestial processions are detailed in the *Chapter on Heavenly Music and Ritual Regalia*; thus, they are not elaborated here.

6. All documents and dispatches follow the *Jade Palace* and *Mysterious Model* formats, supplemented by ancient precedents. Consult the catalogues and apply them as needed. For instance, memorials to the August Thearch use the *memorial* form, while others use the *petition* form. Documents for spirit officials employ the *official dispatch* form.

7. Memorials always refer to the sender as "your servant," while petitions use the sender’s name. Documents from the Heavenly Pivot Institute refer to the office as "this bureau." For cover slips, official notes, and dispatches, the office is termed "this bureau."

8. On memorials and petitions, leave one hand’s width of space at the top and two at the bottom. The paper should be one foot and four inches in height; for other documents, unfolded letter paper is best. Invitation and offering petitions use only petition paper, as prescribed.

9. For the sacred positions listed within memorials, use yellow labels, filling them in at the time.

10. The yellow cover slip on memorials should be three inches and two *fen* in height and two inches and four *fen* in width, or three inches and six *fen* in height and three inches in width as a standard. Write the cover slip in a single column, and after affixing it, sign your name at the seam and apply the seal.

11. For memorials accompanied by a yellow cover slip, use a small yellow label, affixed diagonally below the Tai Sui. This follows ancient practice, though it is seldom used today.

12. For memorials and petitions that list only one sacred position, use a yellow label affixed diagonally. For two, three, or four positions, use a slightly wider yellow label affixed in the center. For three or five positions, the center is the most honorable; for two or four, the right is the most honorable. Write "Before the August One" or "Before the Sacred" in the sacred section, or only the foremost position. For petitions to deities of the lower realms, use white labels, applying them as circumstances require.

13. The outer envelopes of memorials and petitions do not require yellow cover slips or the title "your servant"; simply write the sender’s name. The same applies to the outer envelopes of memorials, petitions, and other documents. If a petition lists many sacred positions, the envelope need only name the foremost.

14. In memorials and petitions to the Thearch, refer to the decree as the "Compassionate Edict of the Dao." For the August Thearch, use "Sagely and Wise Edict"; for the Two Empresses, "Sacred Edict of the Celestial Palace"; for the Three Clarities and Four Emperors, "Your Majesty"; for the Two Empresses, "Your Palace"; for the various August Ones, "Before the August One"; for the Perfected, "Before the Sacred"; and for deities of the lower realms, "Before the Spirit," "Before the Court," and the like.

The **Great Yellow Register Fast** possesses ranks and grades; one must consult established precedents and not act recklessly. Those conducted by scholar-officials and commoners may only be termed "offering rites." **River Chart, Mysterious Numinosity, and other offerings** encompass dozens of names, all offerings. In antiquity, "offering" was another name for sacrifice. No rite surpasses the offering in summoning the Celestial Thearch and assembling the myriad spirits.

1. State-sponsored offerings follow three-day or seven-day rituals. According to the *Lingbao Scripture*’s fast methods, there are twenty-seven days of observance. Du Guangting’s *Offering Grades* lists seventy-two ranks, all employed by the state. As with the *Three Caverns*’ ritual forms, each has its fixed model.

2. When officials, commoners, scholar-officials, or common households conduct offering fasts, they should limit them to one day and night. Some extend them to three or seven days and nights, but this risks irreverence and may instead incur divine censure. Even high officials do not stay overnight in the homes of commoners; how much less would the Supreme Thearch, dwelling in the ninefold heavens, condescend to remain among mortals for three or seven days and nights without returning?

Here follows the translation:

---

The present regulations for offering rituals are as follows: For a one-day ritual, preparations are made in advance, and on the appointed day, the ceremony begins at dawn and concludes at deep night, so as not to risk disrespect toward the sacred. The ritual protocols and standards are recorded in such works as the *Jade Capital* and *Mystic Model Administrative Documents*; when the occasion arises, one may consult them.

1. For the opening of the altar and the establishment of a grand offering, it is best to conduct it within the sacred precincts of a grotto-heaven, blessed land, or Daoist abbey. The altar must be positioned with proper orientation, facing south with its back to the north. If the abbey already has an altar but its orientation is slightly off, one may also set up the altar in a separate, secluded hall according to the prescribed form.

2. When establishing an offering, one must act within one’s means: the wealthy may prepare all necessary items, while the poor may adapt as circumstances allow. The materials for the offering must not be acquired through ill-gotten wealth, nor through haggling over prices, nor through careless preparation when one has the means, nor through forced effort when one lacks them. All such actions lack sincerity and make it difficult to move the divine. If the sponsor of the fast is a household of loyalty and filial piety, and their sincerity is wholehearted, the master may provide such items as dragon silks on their behalf, simplifying all matters. The documents, offerings, and other necessities for the ritual will naturally resonate with the divine.

3. The methods of visualization and the esoteric techniques employed during the offering ritual are recorded in the *Chapter on Qi Transformation and Creation*, while the musical instruments and celestial processional regalia are described in the *Chapter on Celestial Music and Processional Regalia*; these will not be detailed here.

4. All documents and administrative procedures should follow the *Jade Capital* and *Mystic Model* systems, as well as the ancient forms recorded in the administrative manuals. Consult the relevant sections when needed. For instance, memorials presented before the August Thearch use the *memorial* format, while others use the *petition* format; communications with divine bureaus use the *official dispatch* format, and so on.

5. Memorials should be signed with “your subject,” while petitions should bear the sender’s name. Documents from the Celestial Pivot Institute should be titled with the bureau’s name, and preceding documents such as *guan*, *tie*, and *die* should refer to “this bureau.”

6. On memorials and petitions, leave a space of one hand’s width at the top and two hand’s widths at the bottom. The paper should be one foot and four inches in height; for other documents, extended stationery is preferable. Invitation and offering documents for the ritual should use standard petition paper, as prescribed.

7. For the sacred titles within memorials, use yellow labels, to be filled in at the time of writing.

8. The yellow strip affixed to the front of a memorial should be three inches and two *fen* in height and two inches and four *fen* in width, or alternatively three inches and six *fen* in height and three inches in width. Write the text in a single column. After affixing the yellow strip, write the sender’s name at the seam and apply the seal.

9. When a memorial is accompanied by a *yi-huang* (supporting yellow document), use a small yellow label and affix it diagonally below the *Tai Sui* (Year Star) position. This follows ancient practice, though it is rarely used today.

10. For memorials and petitions that list multiple sacred titles, use a yellow label affixed diagonally if there is only one title. For two, three, or four titles, use a slightly wider yellow label affixed in the center. For three or five titles, the central position is the most honorable; for two or four titles, the right is the most honorable. In the sacred section, write “Before the August Presence” or “Before the Sacred Presence,” or simply write the foremost title. For petitions to deities of the lower realms, use white labels, to be applied as appropriate.

11. On the outer envelope of a memorial or petition, do not affix a yellow strip or use the term “your subject”; simply write the sender’s name. The same applies to the outer envelopes of memorials, petitions, and other documents. If a petition lists many sacred titles, only the foremost title should be written on the outer envelope.

12. In memorials and petitions to the Supreme Thearch, refer to “the compassionate decree of the Dao”; to the August Thearch, “the sagely and wise decree”; to the Two Empresses, “the august and compassionate sacred decree”; to the Three Clarities and Four Emperors, “Your Majesty”; to the Two Empresses, “Your Palace”; to the various August Thearchs, “Before the August Presence”; to the Perfected, “Before the Sacred Presence”; and to deities of the lower realms, “Before the Divine Presence,” “Before the Court,” and the like. Those who have received official ranks or titles, such as *ma*, are not permitted to participate in fasting rituals.

13. Even the positions below *Du Jiang* (Chief Cantor) must have received the registers of the Orthodox Unity, Numinous Treasure, and Yang Light traditions before they may participate in the altar rites.

14. When inviting Daoist participants to join the fast, they must be those who are accustomed to prostration and kneeling, content with simplicity, devoted to incense and ritual fires, and free from greed for wealth and property. Only then may they take the oath and ascend the altar. They must match the sincerity of the ritual sponsor, earnestly beseeching the vast heavens to manifest their responsiveness. If they merely pursue the beauty of sound and rhythm without focused devotion, they will not only waste their energy and squander resources but may also incur blame and achieve nothing. The method of conducting rituals depends entirely on the selection of participants; this must not be taken lightly.

15. Daoist youths serving as ritual attendants must first practice the *Bu Xu* hymns, the raising of voices, and the singing of *Hua Xia* and *Yin Ling* until they are proficient. When ascending the altar and circumambulating, they should follow the lead and harmonize with the chanting.

16. When establishing an offering, one must exert utmost sincerity and reverence. Items such as dragon silks, jades, and swords must be of the finest quality. Incense, flowers, oil, and candles—all required supplies—must be pure and immaculate, free from any defilement. If anything is lacking at the time of use, it may instead incur divine censure. In all offerings, single-minded devotion is paramount; dragon silks are of the highest importance, followed by the reverent purity of incense and candles. Any deficiency is a flaw in the ritual. Those who serve in such rites must be especially vigilant.

17. If a coffin remains in the house, one should not open an altar or establish an offering. If the residence is spacious and the funeral is held elsewhere, outside the altar’s precincts, the ritual may proceed. If there are any inauspicious or defiling influences from birth or death that have not been resolved, one must not establish an altar in the household. This must be strictly avoided.

18. When burning incense, do not use fire from the kitchen hearth. When burning paper money and other offerings, do not use oil lamp or candle flames to ignite them.

**Heavenly Heart Mysterious Secret Chapter**
In ancient times, the Primordial Heavenly King suspended a millet pearl over the black soil and commanded the August Person to expound the *Dong Zhang* (Cavern Chapters).

The Most High Lord Lao ascended the Jade Bureau in Chengdu, where he transmitted scriptures and esoteric instructions to Zhang Daoling. The Daoist methods encompass forty-two altars, and the jiao rituals seventy-two grades, disseminated throughout the mortal world to propagate teachings and transformation. Later generations of lineage-bearing Daoists accumulated merit and amassed virtuous conduct, aligning with the Dao to attain perfection. When the heart stirs, the spirit follows; the efficacy of the methods flourishes, and the teachings expand. Thus, the Daoist methods and talismanic writs branched and proliferated, spreading widely through the ages. The arts of the Dao comprise over three thousand ranks, which cannot be exhaustively recorded. Here, only one or two are briefly outlined to convey their general scope.

**Fourteen Altars of Heavenly Jiao**
The *Yellow Emperor’s Jiao Announcement Chapter* states: When mortals perform rites of exorcism, prayer, sacrifice, or ancestral deliverance, or when seeking to avert calamity or cure illness, only those who serve the Dao as Heaven’s adherents may conduct the rites of Heavenly Jiao to petition the celestial realms. For those outside the Daoist tradition who perform exorcisms, prayers, or ancestral deliverance, they are permitted only to summon the city gods, earth deities, local spirits, and officials of the underworld. They must not presumptuously invoke the Celestial Emperor or divine thearchs. Thus, the Thunder Bureau enforces the office of execution and investigation. Should any who are not Daoist adherents of Heaven dare to encroach upon the Celestial Emperor, they shall face the severing of their spirit, the annihilation of their soul, the forfeiture of their allotted lifespan, and the extinction of their years. How could one not stand in awe?

**Major Jiao Rituals**
- **Golden Register Universal Heavenly Grand Jiao**: 3,600 divine stations
- **Jade Register Circumambient Heavenly Grand Jiao**: 2,400 divine stations
- **Yellow Register Multitudinous Heavenly Grand Jiao**: 1,200 divine stations
- **Grand Unity Jiao**
- **Nine Heavens Jiao**
- **River Chart Thirty-Six Heavens Jiao**
- **Jade Casket Alliance of Perfected Jiao**
- **Numinous Treasure Spontaneous Jiao**
- **Cavern Abyss Samādhi Jiao**
- **Disaster-Dispelling Jiao**
- **Fortune and Steed Transfer Jiao**
- **Nine Yous Jiao**
- **Deliverance Jiao**
- **Filial Piety and Ancestral Offering Jiao**

According to the Daoist canon’s established system, the Golden Register, Jade Register, and Yellow Register Jiao each have fixed formats for their sacred stations and ritual configurations. Common jiao rituals comprise forty-eight altars, with memorial offerings and monetary petitions arranged in twenty-four, thirty-six, forty-two, sixty, seventy-two, one hundred twenty, two hundred forty, or three hundred sixty stations. The rites of the jiao mirror the solemnity of worldly protocol. The Dao is magnified through human effort; one must not cling rigidly to convention.

Upon examination, Daoist methods each have their own transmissions and variations. Here, only those commonly practiced in the world are recorded. Additionally, there are methods involving the Thunder Bureau and Fengdu officials, whose names are too numerous to list exhaustively.

**Seven Ranks of Refinement and Salvation Methods**

**Twelve Ranks of the Celestial Marrow Numinous Chapters Great Method**

- *Huntian Method*: This method can open the Celestial Gate, command celestial spirits, halt the sun and detain the moon, transform day into night, summon summer snow and winter thunder.
- *Yidi Method*: This method can point to the earth to make it quake, point to mountains to make them tremble, point to seas to dry them up, draw rivers upon the ground, shift mountains to block seas, and subdue ghosts and spirits.
- *Wansheng Method*: This method ensures boundless victory, transforms grasses and trees, and can turn metal and stone into humans, conceal the body, and hide one’s form.
- *Xianglong Method*: This method enables riding dragons through the sky, transforming objects into dragons, soaring through clouds and mist, and treading upon qi to ascend into the void.
- *Fuhu Method*: This method can subdue tigers, leopards, and all fierce beasts, serpents, and insects.
- *Qiyun Method*: This method can summon clouds and raise mist, generate five-colored auspicious clouds, ride clouds to ascend to heaven, roam the palaces of the sun and moon, and come and go at will.
- *Shengfeng Method*: This method can conjure mighty winds across a thousand miles, raise dust to confront enemies, blow sand and stones, obscure the heavens, and respond to any situation.
- *Furen Method*: This method can cause blades to shatter on their own, render one unharmed by weapons, and make all blades ineffective. When encountering bandits, it can prevent swords from leaving their scabbards and cause bows and crossbows to break, nullifying harm.
- *Bianwu Method*: This method can grow all grasses and trees, ride through the air, and animate wooden figures and wooden beasts.
- *Congbo Method*: This method can turn mountains and hills into lakes, swell rivers and streams, raise towering waves and crashing tides, summon clouds and rain, tread upon waves to cross rivers, and enter water without drowning.
- *Lieyang Method*: This method can generate raging flames and towering fires to burn the heavens, incinerate camps and strongholds, eradicate demons and evil, and with a single passage of divine fire, dispel all misfortunes.
- *Changchun Method*: This method can instantly grow all grasses, trees, grains, melons, fruits, and vegetables, transform earth into gold, turn stone into jade, and conceal the body within the earth.

The preceding twelve methods are sacred texts secretly transmitted by heaven, wondrous arts for transcending the world and leaving the dust behind. They can only be practiced upon receiving transmission from celestial beings. Even if one obtains the written script, it remains empty words on paper, a vain expenditure of effort.

**Daoist Ecclesiastic Ranks and Ming Dynasty Hierarchy**
*Principal Second Rank*: Hereditary Celestial Master of the Han Lineage, Perfected Person.
*Principal Sixth Rank*: Left and Right *Zhengyi* of the Daoist Registry.
*Subordinate Sixth Rank*: Left and Right *Yanfa* of the Daoist Registry, Superintendents of Palaces and Observatories.
*Principal Eighth Rank*: Left and Right *Zhiling* of the Daoist Registry.
*Subordinate Eighth Rank*: Left and Right *Xuanyi* of the Daoist Registry.
*Subordinate Ninth Rank*: *Duji* of the Daoist Discipline Office.
*Unranked*: Vice *Duji* of the Daoist Discipline Office, *Daozheng* of the Daoist Rectification Office, *Daohui* of the Daoist Assembly Office.

**Perfected Persons**
During the Han, Zhang Daoling was granted the title "Perfected Person" as Celestial Master. In the Tang, Mi was bestowed the same title upon his return to the Dao as Chancellor, with an additional rank of Principal First Grade.

**Libationers**
In the reign of King Cheng of Zhou, Tong Bo was appointed Libationer to preside over kinship rites. Later, during King Xuan’s grand sacrifice at the Southern Suburbs, Zhong Shanfu served as Libationer to oversee the ritual. Thus, in subsequent ages, Daoists assumed the office of Libationer to conduct the rites of suburban sacrifices to Heaven, thereby governing the Daoist teachings. This marked the inception of the Libationer’s role among Daoists.

**Daoist Officials**
King Mu of Zhou appointed the Daoist Gao Gongchen as Libationer to worship the Primordial Heavenly Sovereign at the thatched hut of Perfected Person Yin. This was the origin of Daoist officialdom.

**Daoist Registrars**
Emperor Taizong of Song expanded the Daoist registry to include eight officers: Vice Registrar, Supervisor, Chief Seat, and Senior *Tongjiu*, all of whom collectively administered the affairs of the Daoist community.

**Daoist Ennoblement**
During the reign of Emperor Wu of the Later Zhou, Wei Yuansong was enfeoffed as Duke of Shu Commandery—the first instance of a Daoist receiving a noble title. Ye Fashan was later enfeoffed as Duke of Yue during the reign of Emperor Xuanzong.

**Daoist Posthumous Honors**
In the Tang, Wang Zhiyuan was posthumously honored as Master of Ascending Mystery. Ye Fashan was granted the titles Grand Master for Glorious Happiness, Gold and Purple, and Prefect of Yuezhou. These were the first instances of posthumous honors bestowed upon Daoists.

**Daoist Posthumous Titles**
Upon his ascension, Tao Hongjing was posthumously titled Master of Upright Purity by the Liang Emperor. This marked the beginning of such posthumous designations.

**Daoist Discipline**

The Master Laozi said, "One who knows the ancient beginning is said to grasp the Dao’s discipline." Thus, just as the Buddhist clergy established monastic regulations, the Daoist tradition developed its own designations.

**Daoist Titles**
The Yellow Emperor addressed the Herdboy as "Celestial Master"—this was the first instance. Later, during the Han, Zhang Daoling was also called Celestial Master. Daoist names and titles all derive from the principles of Laozi’s *Daodejing*. Characters such as *Dao*, *Mysterious (xuan)*, and *Subtle (miao)*—these are not teachings of China’s native tradition, yet foreign peoples have appropriated them.

**Purple Robes**
During the Tang, Li Bi was born with divine spirit. As a child, his body was so light he could levitate, and his mother often heard celestial music in the air. Fearing he would ascend and depart, she sprinkled his head with juice of scallions and garlic. Later, under Emperor Daizong, he was appointed as chief minister. Li Fuguang, who monopolized power, grew envious of him. Li Bi, recognizing he could not long remain in office, resigned and sought to become a Daoist. The emperor then bestowed upon him a purple robe and golden belt—the first instance of a Daoist being granted purple attire.

**Yellow-Crowned Daoists**
The *Inner Records of the Yellow Emperor* states: "All who serve the Heavenly Dao are called *daoshi* (Daoists)." During the reign of King Mu of Zhou, at the thatched abbey of Master Yin the Perfected, he summoned reclusive worthies to tend the incense and flames in worship of the Heavenly Thearch—this was the first instance of *daoshi* officiating at a temple to venerate the Heavenly Thearch.

The robes and crowns of Daoists are those of the Yellow Emperor, hence the name *yellow-crowned*. What they practice are the affairs of the Yellow Emperor; what they expound is the Dao of Laozi—thus they are called *daoshi*. They do not alter their attire, nor dare they wear anything but the ritual vestments of the former kings. They do not alter their speech, nor dare they utter anything but the words of the former kings.

Those who follow the Dao do not abandon their surnames, for they do not forget their kin; they do not mutilate their bodies, for they do not forget filial piety. Taking the Dao as their teaching, they do not defy Heaven; refusing to serve foreign doctrines, they do not defy their native land. As Chinese people serving the Chinese Dao, they embody the Way of Heaven and follow the advantages of Earth to cultivate themselves. Thus, they can ascend in flight, ride the void and command the winds, transcend the material world in spirit, and ascend to pay homage in the Great Clarity. They attain the wonders of creation, becoming companions of Heaven, able to commune with the numinous powers of Heaven and Earth, align with the virtue of the divine, command ghosts and spirits, summon thunder and lightning, conjure wind and rain, grasp the stars and slay malevolent spirits, dispel plagues and pestilence, and bring about great peace—these are the proven truths since the opening of the world by the Three Sovereigns. Herein lies the manifestation of the Dao as teaching.

**Supervisor of Ceremonies**
Emperor Wen of Sui first appointed Wang Yan, the abbot of Xuandu Abbey, as the official of ritual decorum—equivalent to the present-day role of *Jianzhai* (Liturgist).

**Daoist Registrar**
During the Zhou dynasty, the term was changed to *Daolu* to avoid a naming taboo.

**Supervisor of Rites**
During the reign of Emperor Zhenzong of Song, the position of *Shouzuo Jianyi* (Chief Seat Supervisor of Rites) was established to oversee matters of their respective ranks.

**Senior Seat**
First instituted under Emperor Taizong of Song.

**Ritual Officer**

Zhang Daoling of the Han dynasty first practiced the arts of commanding thunder and deploying ghosts, and those who performed such methods were called *Faguan* (Ritual Officers).

**The Red Script Celestial Statutes**
Only the transgressions of the living against the celestial precepts are recorded; those committed by ghosts and spirits are not, as seen in the *Nüqing Celestial Statutes*.

1. On the seasonal amnesty days of Heaven and Earth, Ritual Officers must not deploy talismans, incantations, or ritual water, nor consult the statutes. Violators shall first suffer themselves, then bring calamity and annihilation to their nine generations.

2. When Ritual Officers perform rituals, they must act in accordance with yang and report in accordance with yin, without beginning earnestly and ending carelessly. Violators shall be annihilated, and calamity shall extend to their nine generations.

3. When Ritual Officers submit petitions for promotion or disciples assume ranks, their names are registered under the Left Judgment Officer. They may then be promoted to Left Grand Judgment Officer, followed by Right Grand Judgment Officer. Violators shall each be sentenced to nine years of penal servitude. Those who knowingly endorse such petitions shall be stripped of their ranks, annihilated, and their crimes shall extend to three generations.

4. If Ritual Officers, Daoists, or laypersons burn incense, submit memorials, or present petitions to the celestial bureaus on the six *wu* days, they shall be annihilated. Those who knowingly violate this shall bring calamity to their nine generations, suffering the "Wind Blade" for ten thousand kalpas without absolution. Those not bearing tally tokens shall be reduced by three ranks.

5. If Ritual Officers, when not slaying ghosts, invoke the phrase *"Hasten as the statute commands!"* at inappropriate times, their lifespans shall be reduced by six years.

6. If Ritual Officers, when inscribing talismans, point the brush tip to the left, they shall be sentenced to nine years of penal servitude. Those who knowingly violate this shall have their lifespans reduced by twelve years.

7. If Ritual Officers, when consecrating water, rotate the water vessel to the left, they shall be sentenced to nine years of penal servitude. Those who knowingly violate this shall have their lifespans reduced by twelve years.

8. If Ritual Officers recklessly reveal orthodox methods to unworthy persons, their lifespans shall be reduced by twelve years.

9. Ritual Officers must not privately worship ghosts and spirits, except for the sacrifices to Ao in the second and eighth months. Violators shall be sentenced to three years of penal servitude; intentional violators shall receive an additional penalty.

10. Wherever Ritual Officers reside, if they encounter floods, droughts, banditry, or other harms afflicting the people, they are permitted to immediately report and petition for celestial punishment of the cunning and malevolent. Violators shall be sentenced to three years of penal servitude. If an officer is dispatched to execute punishment but the offender does not match the reported description, the penalty shall be increased by one degree. If the offender fully matches the report, the officer shall be promoted by two ranks.

11. If Ritual Officers perform rituals carelessly, summoning divine officials and soldiers without selecting proper paper or brushes to write talismans or consecrate water, the celestial authorities shall revoke their sustenance, leaving them impoverished in their lifetimes.

12. If Ritual Officers recklessly mobilize divine officials and soldiers, harming the living, their lifespans shall be reduced by six years.

13. Ritual Officers must not enter the temples of orthodox deities without cause, nor recklessly apprehend such deities using orthodox methods. Violators shall be sentenced to two years of penal servitude. If Ritual Officers enter such temples without proper ceremonial welcome or send-off, the penalty shall not apply.

14. If Ritual Officers receive petitions from the people but fail to act upon them promptly, they shall be sentenced to one year of penal servitude. If the petition does not conform to the proper format, this does not apply.

15. If Ritual Officers, upon encountering private worship of heterodox spirits or licentious ghosts, do not immediately dispatch divine officials to apprehend and punish them according to the statutes, they shall be sentenced to three years of penal servitude.

16. If Ritual Officers observe the fasts and precepts but violate them, they shall be sentenced to seven years of penal servitude.

17.
