When ascending the altar or entering stillness, one should not perform ablutions in a hasty or unclean manner; spittoons should be kept nearby for convenience.

**Feeding Trays for Sentient Beings**
By ancient custom, a tray or platform for sentient beings is placed before the refectory. After each meal, the food that remains is collected by an attendant and then scattered outside. This serves four purposes: first, to offer to the ancestors; second, to present to the earth spirits; third, to sever evil influences—for if this food is not offered, malevolent spirits will vie to invade, poisoning the human body; and fourth, to cultivate compassion, pitying all sentient beings and wishing that they, too, may partake of the Dharma’s flavor and be universally sated. Hence, it is called the *Feeding Tray for Sentient Beings*. Such trays have existed since the time of Zheng Siyuan, Ge Hong, and other masters. They are indispensable even today.

**Bamboo Utensils**

**□** (pronounced *xuàn* in the departing tone): A bamboo vessel, round and shallow. In the Jiang-Huai region, it is used for winnowing and sifting rice and wheat, and is also called a *winnowing basket*. Such implements are indispensable in Daoist mountain retreats.

**Winnowing Basket**: In the Jing-Luo region, these are made of willow, rounded at the back with a hook and square at the front with a flared edge, used for sorting rice and wheat. When the belly is deepened and woven tightly from bamboo, with a broad base and ample depth, the larger ones are called *pángjī*. The people of Chu call them *shāojī*, essential for steaming and cooking, also known as *cuōjī*.

**Brooms**: All halls and temples are swept with fine brooms; no others may be used indiscriminately. Immortals’ households employ brooms made of qilin fur or phoenix feathers, depending on what is available. The most esteemed are made of dragon’s whiskers. In Jiang-Huai, broomcorn millet flowers are commonly used, while in Jing-Luo, broomcorn seedlings are preferred—each following what the land yields. However, for sweeping the main hall, only the finest and smoothest brooms are deemed suitable. Coarser brooms may be used for other temple spaces, but those designated for the main hall must never be employed elsewhere.

**Strainers**: In modern usage, these serve as brush holders. They are also used for sifting medicinal herbs, rice, wheat, and other necessities in mountain retreats.

**□** (pronounced *yù*): In ancient times, this was called *lèyù*, a bamboo vessel shaped like a spiral shell, holding two or three *dou*, used for rinsing rice. Such utensils are indispensable in places where Daoists cultivate the true Way.

**Ritual Vessels**

For all offerings before the Heavenly Worthies during fasts and jiao rites, seasonal flowers and fruits are presented to express utmost devotion. The vessels used must be pure and clean—no defiled, impure, or improper implements may be placed among the ritual offerings. As the *Zhen’gao* states: "When Daoists receive food during a fast, no unworthy person may handle it. Violation invites the punishment of corpse-infestation and spectral torment, as hungry ghosts assail the spirit." This is why ritual vessels are specially designated.

From *The Jade Pivot’s Numinous Writings* and *Discerning the Dao of Immortals*:

The Southern Pole Elder asked the Ageless Master: "Confucians dismiss the notion of immortals as absurd and fantastical, unworthy of discussion. All things under heaven and earth follow the same pattern: flourishing must yield to withering, completion to decay, life to death. How can it be claimed that immortals escape death, matching heaven and earth in longevity? Is this not delusion? To achieve the Dao and ascend in a sudden leap, entering the celestial palaces and joining the ranks of the Perfected—is this not deception? It is like grasping at wind without shadow, seizing reflections impossible to hold, pursuing what cannot exist, and treading paths that cannot be walked. Is this not futile? You are a student of immortality—you must know the truth. Defend it for me."

The Ageless Master replied: "I have heard that among grasses and trees, all sprout in spring and wither in winter—yet the pine and cypress alone remain evergreen. Among birds and beasts, all are born and must die—yet the tortoise and crane alone enjoy long years. If even plants and animals exhibit such exceptions, how much more should humans, the most spiritually endowed of all beings?

Consider further: water is inherently cool, yet in Warm Valley, boiling springs emerge; fire is inherently hot, yet on Xiao Mound, cold flames arise. Stone is a heavy substance, yet in the Southern Sea, floating stones grow; feathers are light, yet in the Eastern Sea, Weak Waters sink them. These are the principles by which heaven and earth generate things—some defy the ordinary.

Again, pheasants transform into clams, sparrows into mussels; earthworms sprout wings, river frogs take flight; water beetles become clams, duckweed decays into maggots; field mice turn into waterfowl, rotting grass into fireflies; Niu Ai became a tiger, the woman of Chu a dragon; turtles transform into tigers, snakes into dragons; mulberry branches become willows, wheat into butterflies; maples take human form, the maiden of Qin turns to stone. These all partake of heaven and earth’s numinous marvels—beyond mortal comprehension, even sages struggle to explain. Such are the wondrous workings of heaven and earth, the principles of transformation.

How much more so for humans, who are endowed with the essence of heaven and earth, mountains and rivers, and the three luminaries? Those who attain the Dao surpass even the insentient grasses and trees!

For example, when sweetened bait is laced with medicine and placed in a fish’s mouth, then boiled in a pot, the unmedicated fish are cooked and eaten, while the medicated one swims in the pot all day as if in a river or sea. When mulberry leaves are dusted with longevity medicine and fed to silkworms, they live for years without aging. When age-arresting medicine is given to newly hatched chicks or puppies, they never grow. When white-restoring medicine is fed to a white dog, its fur turns black within a hundred days. These are the wonders of medicine—how could ordinary people obtain such formulas? This demonstrates the proven efficacy of elixirs in attaining longevity.

Consider also the Yellow Emperor, who refined the Nine Cauldrons on Mount Xing. When the elixir was complete, a yellow dragon descended with flowing whiskers to receive him. The Emperor ascended with eighty-one women, and seventy-one officials clung to the dragon’s whiskers and the Emperor’s bow, rising with him. Today, among the stellar lodges, the seventeen stars of Xuanyuan remain. Gonggong’s minister, Gou Long, who had erred, attained the Dao and ascended to the Southern Pole—now, near the Well and Bow lodges, the single star of the Old Man shines. Chuanxu, minister to Tang, attained the Dao and rode the Tail and Winnowing Basket lodges to become a constellation—today, near the Tail lodge, the star of Chuanxu appears, and near the Woman lodge, the four stars of Xi Zhong. Wang Liang and Zaofu, master charioteers of Zhou, attained the Dao and became stellar ranks—Wang Liang’s five stars array near the Straddler lodge, Zaofu’s five stars near the Rooftop lodge. These are all recorded in celestial texts, visible in the night sky, as clear as the sun and moon, seen by ten thousand eyes, pointed to by ten thousand fingers. How can there be no immortals?

Moreover, consider the principle of transformation: In the Xia dynasty, a woman in the palace transformed into a dragon, then back into a woman. In the Shang, a woman became a man. In the time of King Jing of Zhou, a woman became a man. During the Jianping era of Emperor Ai of Han, a man became a woman, married a husband, and bore a child. During the Jian’an era of Emperor Xian of Han, a man became a woman. These are all instances of transformation.

During the Taihe era of Emperor Ming of Wei, a man in Taiyuan opened an ancient tomb and found a woman in the coffin, still alive at thirty. She was brought out, married, and bore a child. During the Xianning era of Emperor Wu of Jin, Yan Ji of Langye died, but a year later, his voice was heard. When the coffin was opened, he appeared alive. During the Yuankang era of Emperor Hui of Jin, a woman from Liang state was betrothed to a man who was conscripted to the frontier. After a year without his return, her family remarried her, but she died of sorrow and was buried. Years later, her husband returned, opened her tomb, and she revived. He took her as his wife. These are all instances of death followed by rebirth. If the dead can return to life, how much more can the living, who possess the marvels of creation, attain immortality? These accounts are all found in the classics, clearly verifiable.

Now, consider animals: the tortoise lives a thousand years, its shell displaying five colors, with two horn-like bones rising from its forehead. It understands human speech and floats upon lotus leaves."

The thousand-year crane is pure white in color, its brain entirely transformed into cinnabar. It can perch upon trees, while those not yet a thousand years old do not alight on them. The macaque lives eight hundred years, then transforms into an ape; the ape, after five hundred years, becomes a *jue*; the *jue* lives a thousand years without dying. The toad lives three thousand years, as do the *tenghuang* and *jiguang*. The qilin lives two thousand years, while deer and hares live a thousand; when they reach five hundred, their fur turns white. Foxes and wolves live eight hundred years; at five hundred, they gain the ability to transform into humans. The rat lives three hundred years; at a hundred, it turns white and becomes adept at divining by leaning upon people, known as the *zhong*. It can foretell the fortune of the year’s end and events a thousand *li* away. The snake possesses boundless longevity, and all creatures with human faces and avian bodies live ten thousand years. These are all beasts and birds that have received the numinous *qi* of Heaven and Earth, yet they can live for thousands or tens of thousands of years without dying. How much more so for humans, the most spiritually endowed of all beings—could they not attain immortality? These accounts are all recorded in the annals, clearly verifiable. From this alone, the existence of divine transcendents is evident.

The elder said: “From ancient times until now, I have never heard such words.” Upon hearing your explanation, my doubts are dispelled.

**The Rarity of Encountering the Dao**
As stated in the *Zhen’gao*: For a being to escape the three evil destinies and be born as a human is rare. Having been born human, to be male rather than female is rare. Being male, to possess all six senses and four limbs intact is rare. With senses and limbs complete, to be born in the Central Kingdom is rare. Born in the Central Kingdom, to encounter parents and a ruler who favor the Dao is rare. Having met a Dao-favoring ruler, to be born into a Dao-favoring family with a kind and benevolent heart is rare. With a benevolent heart awakened, to believe in the Dao and the attainment of long life is rare. Having believed in the Dao and long life, to encounter the *renchen* era of Great Peace is the rarest of all. How can one not strive with diligence?

**On Karmic Conditions**
The *Jinbi Longhu Gujing* states: Those whose past lives originated among barbarians or were reborn from the karmic retribution of beasts cannot hear the supreme Dao. Those who in past lives did not plant good roots or accumulate meritorious deeds—even if they encounter the true Dao in this life—will find cultivation difficult and loss easy. For their karmic affinity is shallow, shifting with circumstances, and few achieve success. Those who cultivate the supreme, most wondrous Dao of the Perfected do so because of past-life merit, hidden acts of virtue, kindness to others, and rescue from hardship. Heaven and Earth, ghosts and spirits naturally assist and support them, allowing them to meet true adepts and attain realization with ease. Thus, while the Dao may be divided into the orthodox and the heterodox, encountering it is not difficult—preserving it is the true challenge.

Master Zhongli said: “It is easy for humans to seek the Dao, but difficult for the Dao to seek humans”—meaning it is not transmitted to the unworthy. Later seekers of the Dao, though devoted, must guard against the seductions of heretical teachings and heterodox paths. If the heart is not single-minded, one drifts far from the Dao. How can one not be cautious and thorough in this pursuit?

**On Innate Dispositions**
The *Baopuzi* states: If one’s fate is governed by the Star of Life, that person will inevitably favor the Dao of transcendence. Those who favor the Dao will surely attain it. If one’s fate is governed by the Star of Death, that person will not believe in the Dao of transcendence and will not cultivate its practices. Whether one delights in goodness or not is determined by one’s endowment. To alter or deprive this is beyond even Heaven’s power—like metal and stone melted in a furnace or clay vessels shaped in a kiln: though their forms are molded by these means, the sharpness of bronze and iron or the integrity of jars and porcelain depend on what they encounter, not the furnace or kiln that shaped them.

**The Dao’s Orthodoxy and Heterodoxy**
Before Heaven and Earth were separated, the Dao stood alongside them, giving rise to the myriad things and enduring for ten thousand ages without cease. All that humankind employs in daily life is the Dao. Thus it is said: “Heaven gives birth to the multitudes.” And again: “Only Heaven, in its hidden virtue, watches over the people.” Therefore, it establishes the true Dao. The Yellow Emperor proclaimed it, and from the eras of Yao, Yu, Tang, Wen, and Wu to the times of the Duke of Zhou and Confucius, all rulers upheld the Dao of Heaven, rectified human relations, maintained the rites of ruler and minister, the affection of father and son, and the principles of the Three Bonds. This is the Dao of the sage-kings of the Central Kingdom—what is called the orthodox Dao. It was not exclusive to the ages of Yao, Shun, the Zhou, or Confucius. Confucius said: “To seek the obscure and practice the strange—if later generations were to transmit such things, I would not do so.” When heterodox teachings arise, the great principles are obscured—hence, they are called “heretical.”

**Monk Yi’an Questions the Dao**
In the first year of the Xiankang era of Emperor Cheng of Jin, the monk Yi’an asked Tao Kan: “In the world, many follow Buddhism, while few follow the Dao. Why is this?” Tao Kan replied: “The qilin and phoenix do not appear easily; the *moling* and *jia* do not grow often. All things that are rare are precious, while those that are common are base. Among humans, the worthy are always few, and the foolish are always many. The Dao’s teachings lie beyond the five phases and the refining of the furnace. Those who attain it ascend in broad daylight, transcending Heaven and Earth to exist alone, enduring through ten thousand kalpas without decay. Thus, its teachings are profound and abstruse, difficult for the foolish to learn. It is not transmitted to the unworthy, so its followers are always few. As for your teachings, they are merely a single topic—through twenty or thirty, or even forty or fifty years of quiet meditation, one may suddenly awaken, calling it ‘shattering the mass of doubt.’ For the body of form is an illusion, and the greatest joy lies in quiescent extinction. The highest goal is to avoid rebirth in the human realm, attaining the fruit of the Arhat, known as the ‘fruit of no return.’ Though its methods are accessible even to the most foolish and lowly, anyone can practice them—thus, its followers are always many.”

Yi’an said: “This is truly a sound argument.” He then abandoned the monastic life to study the Dao, changing his name to Du Shoujing.

This discourse presents a most reasoned argument, and thus it is recorded here.

*Gou Geng’s Alchemical Trickery*
The *Supreme Elixir Furnace and Tongs* states: “Gou Geng’s method of ‘transmuting straw’—whereby mercury is contracted into base metal—is no different from theft. Not only does it harm oneself, but it harms others even more severely. Thus, it is rightly called ‘the thief’s art,’ and the condemnation is most apt.

Yet some still practice it, willingly embracing the role of thief. Wealth gained through deceit will depart through deceit. I have seen such men squander their entire future, ending their lives in deeper ruin.

When Immortal Ge first began his alchemical studies, he was once taught the method of ‘transmuting straw’—using reagents to refine copper until it turned not only white but also soft and pliable. Later, he observed a Daoist adept crafting drinking vessels from this metal. On the base of each, he had inscribed the words ‘unfit for pawning or sale.’ A guest asked the reason, and the adept replied: ‘This is *straw-silver*. Though my household is poor and I lack proper utensils, I use these as a temporary substitute. But I fear thieves might pawn or sell them, so I mark them to prevent others from falling into ruin.’

In his later years, the Immortal destroyed all such vessels.”

Later practitioners of refinement must all prohibit and abolish such practices.

According to records from the second year of Jingyou in the Song dynasty under Emperor Renzong, the monk Fuqing of Bozhou submitted a memorial: “The disciples of my monastic order have abandoned the ancestral teachings and violated the fundamental precepts of our school. All aspire to the Dao of long life and enduring vision, hoping to ascend to the celestial palaces. They transmit the teachings of the Yellow Emperor and Laozi, and though they retain the name of ‘sitting in meditation,’ they have lost the essence of contemplating the mind and investigating nature. Internally, they secretly adopt the Daoist methods of refining lead and mercury within the body to seek longevity; externally, they practice the arts of ‘green, yellow, and white’ alchemy, coveting wealth and profit. Examining their conduct, it is all nothing more than ‘transmuting straw,’ ‘coagulating mercury,’ and ‘condensing goods’—forging false gold and silver to deceive the world and acquire wealth. This is no different from banditry. They fear neither heavenly retribution, nor royal law, nor divine punishment. How can this be the conduct of those who have left the household life to cultivate the Way?

The practice of the elixir path is inherently the domain of Daoist adepts, as it should be. Yet Daoists, knowing the strict prohibitions and celestial statutes governing alchemical scriptures, dare not engage in such practices. Only we monks secretly pursue them, harboring malicious intent to harm the world. Many have been ruined, their families broken and fortunes lost. As the earlier Confucians said, ‘The treasured teachings of the Daoists have all been stolen by the Buddhists’—this is precisely what they meant. All such practices must be prohibited and abolished.”

The emperor then issued an edict: “If any Daoist dares to entice monks for their wealth and transmit Daoist methods, or if any monk dares to abandon the ancestral teachings, secretly practice Daoist arts, privately forge false gold and silver, engage in ‘transmuting straw,’ ‘coagulating mercury,’ or ‘condensing goods,’ they shall all be exiled to the frontier garrison of Liaoxi to defend against the Khitan.” From this point onward, the transmission of the elixir path to the unworthy ceased.

**On Corpse Liberation**
When a person dies, one must examine their form. If it resembles that of a living person, this is *corpse liberation*. If the feet are not discolored and the skin is unwrinkled, this is also *corpse liberation*. Essentially, if the eyes remain unspoiled and indistinguishable from those of a living person, this is *corpse liberation*. If the hair has fallen out entirely and the bones have lost their form, this too is *corpse liberation*. However, *corpse liberation in broad daylight* is the mark of a transcendent—it does not fall under the category of ordinary *corpse liberation*.

**The Land of Fangzhu**
According to the *True Reports*: Beyond the Eastern Sea, there is a land where the Dao of long life is cultivated, called Fangzhu. Its people regard immortality as the Way and undying as joy. The land of Fangzhu is square, each side measuring 1,300 *li*, totaling 5,200 *li* in perimeter—hence its name. Its height reaches 9,000 *zhang*. There stands the Ever-Bright Great Mountain, and the Night Moon High Mound, each encircling 400 *li*. The land is lush with grasses and trees, bearing flowers and fruits. There grows the *immortal grass*, crimson and radiant, never withering, evergreen for ten thousand years. Those who eat it do not die. There are also sweet spring waters found everywhere; drinking them also confers immortality, and all who dwell there enjoy long life.

In this land resides the Lord of the Blue Emperor, whose palace lies atop the Eastern Florescence Mountain, spanning 200 *li*. Within it dwell celestial transcendent beings, and the palaces of the highest perfected ones are built there, their halls and chambers constructed of interwoven gold, jade, and *juyao* stones. There is also the Dark Cold Mountain, where the outer officials reside, their palaces encircling 200 *li*.

To the east and west of central Fangzhu lie the lesser Fangzhu lands, each 3,000 *li* distant from the greater Fangzhu. These lesser lands are also square, each side measuring 300 *li*, with a perimeter of 1,200 *li*. Each has its own palace of the Lord of the Blue Emperor, where celestial perfected beings reside.

It is said that these lands have existed since the beginning of creation, though none know their age. The mountains produce spirit birds and spirit beasts, none of which are known by name. The greater Fangzhu lies southeast of Kuaiji, 70,000 *li* distant. To the northeast, one finds the Scalding Valley and the Land of the Fusang Tree, another 60,000 *li* beyond Fangzhu.

In the land of the western lesser Fangzhu, many follow the Buddhist path. They erect pagodas carved from gold and jade, some rising hundreds of *chi* in layered towers. The people there are exceedingly filial and do not die, a result of consuming the *immortal grass*. They all ingest the essences of the Five Stars and the radiance of the sun and moon—by day, the light of the sun, and by night, the brilliance of the moon. They study the *Returning to the Hidden* of the Xia dynasty and use it to achieve flight.

In the eastern lesser Fangzhu, rare treasures abound, wondrous and numinous. There are jade wine and golden nectar. The Lord of the Blue Emperor stores celestial treasures here, and many transcendent beings dwell in this land. They eat the *immortal grass* and drink this wine and nectar, their bodies taking on the hue of gold and jade. Often, they play the *Nine Spirit Flutes* for their own amusement. The sound of a skilled flutist carries for forty *li*. The flutes have thirty holes, the bamboo measuring two to three *chi* in length. When nine flutes play in unison, the hundred beasts dance in joy, and phoenixes gather in flocks, their cries and dances harmonizing with the flute music—this is the music of that land, vastly different from the Buddhist practices of the Western Hu.

The Western Hu’s method involves blowing great conch horns and striking great dharma drums, their music unlike that of Fangzhu, and their teachings even more so. The *Nirvana Sutra* states: “Birth and extinction are extinguished; quiescence is joy.” Thus, they regard life as illusion and death as joy. The people of Fangzhu, however, regard life as joy and death as calamity. Therefore, they speak of *Buddhist teachings* but not of *Buddhist Dao*.

**From the *True Reports***
According to the *Comprehensive Examination of Literature*: Beyond the Eastern Sea lies Floating Swan Mountain. During the reign of Emperor Wu of Liang, the mountain drifted to the eastern sea of Zhejiang. Upon it dwelled over three hundred female transcendent beings, each three to four hundred years old, along with two masters, each a thousand years old. The mountain produced vermilion grass, which they wove into mats and presented to the emperor. They said that within the grass dwelled red birds, which the emperor ordered to be painted—these were revealed to be vermilion phoenixes. After ten days, the mountain floated away again.

The *barbarians* revere the Dao.

The state of Joseon, since King Wu enfeoffed Jizi there, retained the rites, music, institutions, attire, culture, medicine, shamanism, divination, and augury of the Central Kingdom. As the saying goes among the Zhou people, "Half of the ten thousand Shang merchants crossed the Liao River"—this refers to the five thousand seven hundred and eighty-eight Chinese who accompanied Jizi to that land. To this day, its rites, music, institutions, *Classic of Poetry*, and cultural artifacts endure, preserving much of the Central Kingdom’s legacy. It cannot be spoken of in the same breath as the *barbarian* states.

Alas, the secrets of the Heavenly Dao were not transmitted to lands of foreign tongues, and thus it lacks Daoist teachings.

According to the *Mirror of the Dao*: There was a man of Silla named Kim Gakgi, who was ashamed of his country’s coarse language and *barbarian* customs. He entered the Central Kingdom to study its speech and the Dao of the Yellow Emperor and Laozi for twenty-four years. Suddenly, he encountered an extraordinary person who bestowed upon him the essential secrets of the Heavenly Heart and the Dao of ascension and transformation. Thereupon, he devoted himself to the wondrous Dao, reciting the various scriptures of Daoist transcendents without cease for nine years. The Heavenly Emperor conferred upon him a sacred mandate, and he concealed himself in Mount Zhongnan. In the eleventh year of the Dazhong era of Emperor Xuanzong of Tang, on the fifteenth day of the second month, he submitted a memorial to the court, stating: "Your servant has received a decree from the Jade Emperor to ascend as Attendant of the Yingwen Terrace. Next year, on the fifteenth day of the second month, your servant shall ascend to Heaven." The emperor marveled at this and dispatched a court attendant to observe. On the day of his ascension, tens of thousands of residents gathered to witness, all hearing the voices of divine beings in the sky, who declared:

"The King of Silla upholds benevolence and gentleness, never bullying the weak or seizing the lands of neighboring states. He harbors no deceit toward great nations, nor does he obstruct tribute to the Central Kingdom. He does not favor warfare or the slaughter of living beings. Kim Gakgi is a clansman of the King of Silla. By decree of the Supreme Emperor, he shall ascend in broad daylight as Attendant of the Yingwen Terrace."

The states of Silla, Joseon, Tamna, and Baekje, all along the eastern shores of the sea, each have kings to govern them, all under the jurisdiction of the Eastern Florescence Emperor Lord. Any powerful state that seizes their lands to make them subordinate prefectures, obstructs tribute to the Central Kingdom for its own gain, or favors warfare and the slaughter of living beings shall, after death, suffer in the Nine Dark Realms, their bodies tormented by wind and blades, condemned for ten thousand kalpas without pardon. Those who invade others’ lands shall have their descendants struck by premature misfortune, and upon death, their souls shall become dogs in those lands, passing through the executioner’s block to repay their debts for a hundred generations. Aside from the retribution exacted by the mountain and river spirits of the various states, there is no absolution. Only the people of Silla, who have rendered service to the world, may ascend to the heavenly courts.

As the words faded, suddenly the air resounded with the music of flutes and drums, and phoenixes and cranes danced in flight. Banners and canopies descended from the sky to welcome him, and he ascended to Heaven. From this, it is evident that Silla, Joseon, Baekje, and Tamna, all along the eastern shores of the sea, receive the pure and numinous *qi* of Heaven and Earth and are thus capable of cultivating the Dao—this is the proof.

Master Huangfu said: "Along the eastern shores of the sea, the eight states of Goguryeo, Tamna, Silla, and Baekje have lands and springs connected to the geomantic veins of Penglai. Their people are all capable of cultivating the Dao, and those who study it may attain longevity and enduring vision. Alas, they have forsaken the land of the East’s vital *qi* and the fount of immortality, instead embracing the Western teachings of metal’s stern, desolate, and extinguishing *qi*, regarding death as joy and life as illusion. Due to metal overcoming wood, they have lost the true immortal Dao and cannot attain longevity or enduring vision. Only Kim Gakgi of Silla understood that the Eastern lands possess the *qi* of immortals, belonging to spring and water, the realm of Heaven and Earth’s generation, the direction from which the sun rises—all places where the Dao may be cultivated. Thus, he entered the Central Kingdom to seek a master and inquire into the Dao, and ultimately ascended in broad daylight."

The Azure Cloud Elder said: "The *barbarian* states are meager in fortune, and their people, having no prior cultivation or merit, possess shallow karmic roots and cannot be born in the Central Kingdom. Thus, their languages are unintelligible, and their Dao cannot be conveyed through written or spoken words. It is transmitted only mouth to mouth, heart to heart, requiring the heart to merge with the wondrous and the Dao to harmonize. Because their languages are unintelligible, it cannot be transmitted."

**The Uighur Teachings**
According to the *Scripture of the Uighur Möngke Temür’s Teachings*, translated into Chinese as the *Heavenly Scripture of the Most High Lord Lao’s Journey to the Western Regions to Convert the Barbarians and Attain the Dao*, it states: "The Dao of the filial son lies in loyalty and filial piety. Once one understands loyalty and filial piety, one must know whence the body comes—it is the legacy of one’s parents, forming the child’s body. Having this body, one must understand the principles of filial piety. In serving one’s lord, one must fulfill the duties of a subject, never daring to defy the Heavenly Dao. The great Dao is singular, governing the transformations of the One Origin, and is the lord of Heaven, Earth, sun, moon, stars, and the myriad things. Vast and boundless, most honored and noble, it is the limitless and unparalleled Dao, encompassing all phenomena. The myriad teachings and thousand schools all emerge from it, making it the mother of Heaven, Earth, and the myriad things. As for humanity, it is born of Heaven and treads upon Heaven’s path, knowing only one Heaven. Thus, they revere Heaven as their teaching."

A gatha says:
There is a thing before Heaven and Earth,
Formless, originally quiescent and empty,
Yet it is the lord of the myriad phenomena—
The Heavenly Dao is naturally luminous.

From this, it is clear that the teachings established by the Most High, even in *barbarian* lands and regions of foreign tongues, universally transform them with benevolence and instruct them in righteousness, as seen here. Thus, among the Uighur who cultivate this teaching, there are those who live for three hundred years—this is the proof. Therefore, the Uighur do not defy Heaven but uphold its teachings. Their teaching acknowledges only Heaven and no other gods. Each day at dawn and dusk, they face Heaven, calling out to it and seeking blessings. They touch it with their hands, stroke their faces, and press it to their chests, believing that Heaven bestows fortune upon them.

The Uighur’s teaching of revering Heaven is thus. In the *Discourse on Transforming the Barbarians* composed by Emperor Lizong of the Song, it is stated:

I have examined the books of the Ru and Dao traditions that the Hu people sought to destroy. The Hu deeply resent the claim that Laozi transformed the barbarians, asserting that Laozi was born in the reign of King Ding, while the Buddha was born before Laozi’s departure through the pass, during the time of King Zhao—contradicting the records in Chinese Ru texts. Yet when I consult the Ru classics, the *Comprehensive Mirror* records that during the reign of King You, the Luo River ran dry, and Laozi lamented its desiccation, all of which is documented in the historical annals. King You was the ten-generations-removed ancestor of King Ding, predating him by a full ten reigns. How, then, could Laozi’s name have appeared earlier?

Furthermore, the *Biography of Laozi* compiled by Liu Xiang of the Han states that Laozi served the Shang as the Keeper of Archives for the Lord of the West. The Ru classics also record: "Lao Peng was a worthy minister of the Shang." Additionally, the scriptures of the Huihui consistently document the deeds of Laozi transforming the barbarians and attaining the Dao. From this, it can be conclusively argued that Laozi was born in the Shang.

At that time, the one who received the Mandate of Heaven to rule all under Heaven was called the Heavenly King. The Zhou, by virtue of King Wen’s power, were favored by August Heaven and encompassed the Four Seas as lords of the world. Their virtue and beneficence transformed all directions, so that none failed to submit. Thus, the myriad regions came to court, all bathed in the Son of Heaven’s power, for it was the reach of his grace that brought them. Laozi, as a minister of the Zhou Heavenly King, by the transformative power of the Son of Heaven’s virtue, departed westward through Hangu Pass and spread his teachings among the Qiang and the peoples of the west. All their governance and instruction originated from the Central Kingdom. As for those who speak of cultivating and studying the Dao, the very term *Dao* was established by Laozi. Since they speak of cultivating the Dao, it is undoubtedly Laozi’s transformation—could they not be Laozi’s disciples?

The *Doctrine of the Mean* states: "Cultivating the Dao as a teaching." To speak of cultivating the Dao is to cultivate Laozi’s teaching. What further doubt remains?

As for the Buddha, his birth is attested in the *Wen Xuan*, compiled by Emperor Wu of Liang and his heir, Crown Prince Zhaoming. The text states: "The two Zhuangs of Zhou and Lu personally witnessed the omen of the night’s radiance"—referring to the stars’ disappearance. "The two Ming of Han and Jin together adorned the embellishments of cinnabar"—referring to the rise of his teaching. It records that the Buddha was born in the ninth year of King Zhuang of Zhou, corresponding to the seventh year of Duke Zhuang of Lu. His teaching first arrived during the reign of Emperor Ming of Han and flourished in the time of Emperor Ming of Jin. Thus, it is said: "Born in the two Zhuangs, flourished in the two Mings." This was Emperor Wu of Liang’s decree, recorded in the Ru classics as evidence for all under Heaven and all generations—a universal judgment that cannot be altered. Is this not the will of Heaven at work? Thus, the traces of China’s sages’ births and the matter of transforming the barbarians are aspects of the Heavenly Dao that cannot be erased!

Alas, how arduous! Now, upon examining the teachings of Daoism and Buddhism, the origins of the *Scripture on Laozi’s Transformation of the Barbarians* began with Wang Fu. Initially ordained as a monk, his unparalleled intelligence aroused the envy of his fellow clerics, who attempted to poison him, but he survived. He then let his hair grow, donned the yellow cap, and rose to the rank of libationer. Due to his enmity with the Buddhist clergy, he altered the ancient version of the *Transformation of the Barbarians Scripture*, adding spurious claims. They mutually suppressed one another, shifting Laozi’s birth to the reign of King Ding and the Buddha’s birth to the time of King Zhao, placing it before Laozi’s western transformation and departure through the pass. From this, the origins of the *Scripture*’s fabrication were not of recent making.

I contend that the matter of transforming the barbarians cannot be taken on faith. The books of the Daoist and Buddhist traditions must be verified against the Ru classics to discern who established the teachings and who was transformed by whom. The evidence is found in the *Comprehensive Geography: Barbarian Regions*, the *Wei略: Western Rong Chronicles*, the *Sui History: Western Regions Annals*, Pei Kai’s *Memorial to Emperor Huan of Han* and his annotated *Records of the Two States*, Cui Yuanshan’s *Lai Xiang Ji*, the biographies of Huangfu Mi and Ji Kang, Fan Ye’s *Book of Later Han*, Song Yun’s *Southern Yunnan Travelogue*, the *Veritable Records of Emperor Taizong of Tang*, the *Memorial of the Eight Scholars*, the eulogies of successive emperors, the prefaces of Emperor Xuanzong of Tang and Emperor Guangzong of Song—all of which are recorded in the Ru texts and corroborated by the Huihui scripture *Musa’lima*. The truth or falsity of these matters shines as brightly as the sun and stars; they cannot be concealed. This is the universal judgment of all under Heaven and all generations—clear as day.

Alas, what more need I say? Comparing the teachings of the Buddha, they guide with compassion and love; the teachings of the Yellow Emperor, they guide with benevolence and righteousness; the teachings of Laozi, they guide with Dao and virtue, and expound loyalty and filial piety; the teachings of Confucius, they guide with ritual and music, and expound the fundamental norms. The essence of these three teachings in civilizing the world lies in nothing more than a single goodness—how can they be so envious of one another’s arts as to attack each other? Though the Yi and Xia differ, and customs vary, their pursuit of goodness is one and the same.

Before the Han dynasty, China knew only the two teachings of Ru and Dao. The Ru scholars even regarded Yang Zhu and Mo Di as heterodox and attacked them. By the Song dynasty, they also deemed the teachings of the Luo and Lian schools as "false learning," for each established its own sect and did not follow the path of the former kings. Indeed, the sagely teachings must contain profound principles. Even among the disciples of Confucius, it was said that principles were not fully fathomed and knowledge was not exhausted—if even the sages were thus, how can mediocre scholars presume to comprehend? How can they envy others’ strengths, slander the Heavenly Emperor, disparage Confucius and Laozi, and harbor resentment? This is nothing but a path to chaos—is it not so?

**Wu Cheng, Academician of the Yuan, Remonstrates Against Praying for Blessings in the Netherworld**
According to the *Collected Works of Wu Caolu*, in brief: In the third year of Zhizhi of Emperor Yingzong, the transcription of the golden-script Buddhist sutras was completed. The emperor then commanded the Left Chancellor of the Secretariat, Susu, to issue an edict ordering Academician Wu Cheng to compose a preface for the sutras. The imperial decree stated: "The transcription of the sutras is dedicated to three purposes: praying for blessings for the departed sagely emperors, seeking eternal mandate from Heaven for the ruler, and praying for the welfare of the people. A preface shall be written for these three matters."

Wu Cheng replied: "Your Majesty’s intent in transcribing the sutras—for the state and the people—is a most noble act. However, as for praying for blessings in the netherworld, I remain ignorant of its efficacy. The Buddhist doctrine of cause and effect has never been misleading since ancient times, yet the foolish among the people delight in hearing it. Since the founding of this dynasty, how many times have sutras been transcribed for such prayers! If the deliverance proves ineffective, then the principle is nonexistent; if it proves effective, then it slanders one’s ancestors. To compose such words would be unworthy of posterity."

The Left Chancellor said: "This is the emperor’s command. Sir, please await His Majesty’s return and present your case personally."

When Emperor Yingzong arrived, Liulin was the Censor-in-Chief. Tie Shi assassinated the emperor in his traveling tent. Upon ascending the throne, Wu Cheng wept before the new emperor, saying: "Praying for blessings led to swift self-destruction, dying at the hands of treacherous ministers—this was the fate of Emperor Wu of Liang and Emperor Xiang of Qi. The futility is evident. To pray for the deliverance of ancestors is to wish them rebirth in the Western Rong lands rather than in the Central Kingdom—truly a laughingstock for all generations." The emperor then commanded Daoist priests to perform the *Qishou* ritual for longevity, declaring: "I, having inherited the accumulated virtue of my ancestors and the celestial mandate, have received the bright decree of Heaven to rule as lord of the Central Kingdom and possess the Four Seas. I wish to ascend with the people into the realm of longevity, sparing them from the calamity of premature death, and fulfilling the virtue of Heaven’s completion. The Lord on High cherishes life—may this prayer be granted."

He also established the *Jianzu* ritual for ancestral deliverance, declaring: "I have heard that the human form is hard to obtain, and birth in the Central Kingdom is rare. My ancestors were born in the northern deserts and received the mandate of Heaven. I was born in the Central Kingdom. Former sages all prayed for their ancestors’ rebirth in the Western Rong lands, but now, through my prayers, I wish the spirits of the Nine Temples to ascend to the celestial gates, not to be reborn in the Western Rong." Thereupon, he ordered that in every province, on festival days and the emperor’s birthday, Daoist priests should pray to Heaven to seek longevity for the Son of Heaven, blessings for the people, and the ascension of ancestors to Heaven. The rituals of *Jianba* (deliverance) and *Xishou* (prayer for longevity) were entrusted to Daoist recorder Hao Chongxiao for revision, and the new rites were disseminated throughout the land. Henceforth, all state rituals were to follow this principle.

**Oral Instructions on Cultivating Immortality**
When consuming medicinal substances, avoid garlic, pomegranate seeds, pig’s liver, and dog’s head meat. Complete abstention is the highest path for Daoist priests. One must not consume pork or dog meat while engaging in bedroom arts, for this nullifies the efficacy of the medicine. Each pound consumed diminishes one’s lifespan by a hundred days—beware! (Recorded by a disciple of Peng Zu.)

When taking divine medicines, never face north—this is a great taboo. On *hai* and *zi* days, do not spit, lest one lose essence and qi, shortening one’s lifespan and rendering the medicine’s potency as dust. (From *Accounts of Divine Immortals*.)

Daoist priests seeking immortality must not consort with women. A single encounter drains a year’s medicinal efficacy. Even without consuming medicine, engaging in bedroom arts reduces one’s lifespan by thirty years. (From *Accounts of Divine Immortals*.)

**Oral Instructions of the Green Youth Lord**
Daoist cultivators consuming food must avoid bloody substances. Eating them prevents the expulsion of the Three Corpses; only dried meat is permissible. (See Ge Hong’s *Inner Chapters*.)

**Methods for Daoist Cultivators**
When ill, close your eyes and inwardly visualize, using the fire of the heart to burn the body. Preserve the entire body, making the essence as if tangible—the illness will be cured. If pain persists, direct the fire to that spot, and it will surely take effect. (From *Accounts of Divine Immortals*.)

Those cultivating the Dao and seeking immortality must not look upon corpses, for it severely harms the spirit and disrupts qi. Only rulers, teachers, and beloved parents may be attended in death out of necessity. Thus, when Daoist priests pass away, they do not serve kings or nobles—this would be lacking in loyalty. To remain solitary and aloof is to lack companionship. Only for parents, teachers, and masters must one attend their funerals, enduring the utmost grief and risking harm to one’s life. If one is harmed by such sorrow, it is as if one had never been harmed at all. I keep this secret and transmit it orally.

From *Accounts of Divine Immortals*:

All who study immortality must observe the taboo days: the ninth day of the third month, the second day of the sixth month, the sixth day of the ninth month, and the third day of the eleventh month. On these days, if one enters the chamber, one must not see women. Should the Six Corpses stir, the hidden blood will scatter and surge, the Three Hun souls lose their anchor, the spirit wither, and the qi depart—accumulating until death. The reason for avoiding these days is not merely to restrain reckless indulgence, but specifically to pacify the Palace of Women.

The Palace of Women resides in *shen* (the ninth earthly branch), while the Palace of Men resides in *yin* (the third earthly branch). *Yin* and *shen* clash, and their mutual punishment brings harm. On these days, the male and female Three Corpses emerge from the red pupils of the eyes—the female corpse beckons the male, the male corpse beckons the female. Disaster and misfortune come and go, depleting the spirit and diminishing life. Though one may not perceive it, the body’s form is already damaged, for the Three Corpses wage war within the eyes, and blood flows into the Mud Pill Palace.

Even if a woman is most beloved or a wife most cherished, one must resolutely avoid facing her on these days. The former masters attained immortality solely by observing this practice.

Even kinfolk are not exempt—those without intent are no exception. You must be vigilant.

All Daoist practitioners, when sleeping at night, should lie on their side, visualizing the Dipper covering their body. When seated, they should envision the sun within the Mud Pill Palace and the moon at the navel. Before sleep, they must clasp their hands in the Double Thunder Seal, hold their breath, and contract the lower body nine times, as if restraining the urge to relieve themselves, before drifting off. Upon waking, they should repeat this practice, bending their legs to prevent the loss of essence—this must be observed with utmost care.

On days such as *jiǎyín* (Wood Tiger) and *gēngshēn* (Metal Monkey), when the corpse-spirits vie in chaos and the spirit is restless and defiled, one must not share a bed with a spouse, for this is greatly taboo.

Those who dwell in mountains to cultivate truth and study the Dao must be cautious in speech, for mountain spirits and myriad spirits often test them. When sleeping at night, they should close their eyes and visualize the Eye Youth within the Mud Pill Palace, directing their inner gaze to the body’s spirits, thereby attaining long life and ascending to heaven. The immortal Liu Jing once used this method for protection. *(From the* Biographies of Divine Transcendents.*)*

When traveling in the mountains, one must wear a cloud hat wrapped in black silk to shield against wind, sun, dust, and sand. In winter, a snow scarf and deerskin robe are worn. Beneath the left armpit, a deerskin pouch must hold medicinal provisions, cinnabar, and life-saving remedies—these must never be lacking. When walking, one may carry a *Zhenling* staff to repel malevolent qi, or ride a mule while a disciple follows, bearing the staff. Such is the bearing of a Daoist, distinct from the ways of the vulgar world.

Those dwelling in mountains may wear a cloth headband, known in the俗 as the "one-stroke kerchief," wrapping a single strip around the head, paired with hempen sandals. A long sash is the attire of reclusive mountain scholars.

When gathering herbs in the mountains, one must halt a hundred paces from the mountain, first retreat a hundred paces, then ascend with reversed steps. Thus, mountain spirits will not harm the traveler, all evil will flee in submission, and every poison will hide away. *(From the* Biographies of Divine Transcendents.*)*

When passing through mountains or visiting sacred shrines, one should visualize within the mouth a true person named Red Numinous Elder, attended by two jade maidens—one named Hua Zheng, the other She Jing. The Elder wears a crimson gauze robe, while the maidens are clad in yellow above and below. Upon visualization, one must shout: "Spirits of the shrine, hasten forth! Let all evil be delivered to the Red Numinous Elder to be slain. Let the myriad spirits retreat a thousand *li*!" This is the method of the Three Heavens’ vanguard for capturing ghosts. *(From the* Sword Classic *and* Biographies of Divine Transcendents.*)*

When traveling at night, one should first silently recite the Golden Light Mantra, visualizing one’s own radiance enveloping the body. Recite the Heavenly Peng Mantra, frequently click the teeth, and press the two fingers against the philtrum above the nostrils—thus, no malevolent ghost will dare approach. If a ghost appears, declare: "By the decree of the Heavenly Emperor, I oversee the Six Heavenly Palaces of Fengdu. The first is the Palace of Zhou’s Absolute Yin, the second the Palace of Tai’s Slaughter and Solemn Affairs, the third the Palace of Mingchen’s Endurance and Martial Might, the fourth the Palace of Tianzhao’s Sinful Qi, the fifth the Palace of Zongling’s Seven Transgressions, and the sixth the Palace of Gansi’s Continuous Grievances. Whoever dares violate me shall face the statutes of Nüqing—no pardon shall be granted!" Then click the teeth again and recite the Heavenly Peng Mantra, and the ghost will flee a hundred *li*, while demons will not dare intrude.

Daoist practitioners must ensure that when cutting their hair, eating, or handling shoes, pillows, or bedding, no unenlightened person witnesses their haircut, interferes with their meal, moves their shoes, or uses their pillow or bedding. For the ghosts dwelling within the corporeal forms of the vulgar will encroach upon one’s spirit. Thus, Daoists retreat to mountains and forests, secluding themselves to distance themselves from the clamor and filth of the world, severing worldly affairs—all to prevent external things from violating their lives. Guard this well! *(From the* Biographies of Divine Transcendents.*)*

Morning Cultivation on Auspicious Occasions Chapter

**Chapter on Morning Cultivation During Auspicious Occasions**

**First Month**
On the **First Day**, the Heavenly Central Festival Assembly occurs. The Primordial Heavenly Worthy ascends to the Nine Dark Heavens, presenting the *Taiyi Golden Writ* to the Heavenly Thearch. The Most High Lord Lao manifests, and the August Heavenly Emperor leads the gods of heaven and earth in paying homage to the Three Pure Ones. The Seven Star Lords of the Eastern Palace descend, while Master Xulai Le transmits scriptures to the Perfected Lord Ge Xuan upon Mount Shangyu in Kuaiji.

On the **Second Day**, the Heavenly Bureau’s *Lüesheng* descends.

On the **Third Day**, the Great White Star and the Northern Dipper descend.

On the **Fourth Day**, the Founding Festival, the Jade Dawn Great Dao Lord ascends to the Jade Radiance Numinous Chamber and surveys the Four Directions of the world.

On the **Fifth Day**, the Two Perfected, Deng Baiyu and Wang Zhongfu, ascend together.

On the **Sixth Day**, the Jade Pivot Assembly is established to ensure peace for the month.

On the **Seventh Day**, known as the Superior Assembly Day, one may observe abstinence. The Perfected Warrior descends; the Four Dipper Thearchs descend to purify their conduct, and Perfected Gan ascends.

On the **Eighth Day**, the Southern Dipper descends.

On the **Ninth Day**, the Three Primordial Ladies of the Great Simplicity pay homage to the Perfected.

On the **Tenth Day**, the Heavenly Worthy of Longevity and Life-Preservation descends.

On the **Eleventh Day**, the Heavenly Worthy of Disaster-Dispelling and Calamity-Resolving descends.

On the **Thirteenth Day**, the Three Primordials gather the Sages.

On the **Fourteenth Day**, the Three Officials descend.

On the **Fifteenth Day**, the **Upper Prime Festival**, the Heavenly Official bestows blessings. The August Emperor of Primordial Virtue manifests; the Western Dipper Thearch descends. The Three Officials of Heaven, Earth, and Water pay homage to Heaven. The Perfected Lord of Upholding Virtue and Protection descends; the Perfected Lord of Assisting Life and Mandate is born. The Perfected Lord of Orthodox Unity and Tranquil Response is born. The Perfected Lord Zhang Lingyuan of Golden Essence Mountain ascends. The innumerable hosts of the Ten Heavenly Divine Officers, divine beings, and soldiers, along with the lofty Perfected and wondrously accomplished Realized Ones, descend together to the human realm to assess and determine karmic rewards and punishments.

On the **Eighteenth Day**, the occasion for the Three Primordials’ Inner Memorial.

On the **Nineteenth Day**, the Holy Mother of the Northern Yin descends; the Five Pestilence Spirits spread disease.

On the **Twentieth Day**, the Southern Dipper Star Lord descends.

On the **Twenty-First Day**, the Heavenly Assistant Vice Marshal descends.

On the **Twenty-Second Day**, the Hereditary Celestial Master, Perfected Lord Zhang, ascends; the Three Corpses Spirits memorialize karmic rewards and punishments.

On the **Twenty-Fifth Day**, the Heavenly Peng descends; the Northern Dipper begins its procession.

On the **Twenty-Sixth Day**, the Northern Dipper continues its procession; the Upholding Sage descends.

On the **Twenty-Seventh Day**, the Northern Culmen and Northern Dipper descend.

On the **Twenty-Eighth Day**, the Perfected Lord Xu is born.

On the **Twenty-Ninth Day**, the Northern Yin descends.

**Second Month**
On the **First Day**, the Heavenly Correct Festival, also called the **Central Harmony Festival**. The Perfected Lord of Upholding Virtue and Protection descends. The Perfected Lord Wang of Penetrating Emptiness and the Perfected Lord Guo of Wondrous Response and Vast Distance ascend together.

On the **Second Day**, the Perfected Lord Bao Yi encounters the Three August Ones and the Heavenly Worthy of Salvation from Suffering on Mount Song; the Heavenly Bureau’s *Lüesheng* descends.

On the **Third Day**, the Northern Culmen and Northern Dipper descend.

On the **Fourth Day**, the Southern Dipper Star Lord descends; the Six Bureaus descend.

On the **Fifth Day**, the Northern Culmen Heavenly Peng Marshal of the Great Origin descends.

On the **Sixth Day**, the Eastern Culmen Eastern Flower Emperor Lord is born. On this day, the Jade Pivot Assembly is established to ensure peace for the month.

On the **Seventh Day**, the Western Dipper Upholding Sage Perfected Lord descends; the Northern Dipper begins its procession.

On the **Eighth Day**, the **Fragrant Spring Festival**. The Most High Jade Dawn Great Dao Lord ascends to the Jade Radiance Numinous Chamber and surveys the Four Directions of the world. The Three Primordial Ladies of the Great Simplicity pay homage to the Perfected. The Perfected Warrior descends; the Southern Dipper descends; the Heavenly Thearch tours the Eastern Well.

On the **Ninth Day**, the Eastern Dipper descends; the Northern Yin descends.

On the **Tenth Day**, the Heavenly Worthy of Longevity and Life-Preservation descends.

On the **Eleventh Day**, the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion and Great Mercy universally saves all beings of the Three Realms from suffering; the Heavenly Worthy of Disaster-Dispelling and Calamity-Resolving descends.

On the **Twelfth Day**, the Three Perfected—Yin Qianzi, Zhang Shisheng, and Li Fanghui—ascend together.

On the **Thirteenth Day**, the Perfected Lord Ge of the Middle Prime is born.

On the **Fourteenth Day**, the Perfected Lord Lüqiu Fangyuan ascends.

On the **Fifteenth Day**, the **True Prime Festival**. The Grand Master of the Three Teachings, the Most High Lord Lao, the August Emperor of Primordial Virtue and Dao, is born; the Western Dipper descends.

On the **Sixteenth Day**, the Heavenly Bureau’s *Lüesheng* Grand Master descends.

On the **Nineteenth Day**, the Northern Yin descends.

On the **Twenty-Third Day**, the Perfected Lord of Upholding Virtue and Protection descends; the Northern Dipper begins its procession.

On the **Twenty-Fifth Day**, the Perfected Lord Jin of Silla ascends.

On the **Twenty-Sixth Day**, the Northern Dipper continues its procession; the Perfected Lord Xu of Empty Tranquility and Primordial Simplicity is born.

On the **Twenty-Seventh Day**, the Northern Culmen and Northern Dipper descend.

On the **Twenty-Ninth Day**, the Holy Mother of the Northern Yin descends.

On the **Thirtieth Day**, the Perfected Lord of Great Compassion, Great Mercy, and Great Wisdom manifests.

**Third Month**
On the **First Day**, the Nine Mounds Earth Sage Lord ascends to the *Boli Dahe* Heaven to memorialize the names of the immortals who study the Dao and virtue in the Nine Lands to the Lords of the Four Heavens.

On the **Second Day**, the Heavenly Bureau’s *Lüesheng* descends.

On the **Third Day**, the **Day of Expelling Evil**. The Perfected Warrior of the Northern Heavenly Pillar is born. The Perfected Lord Ge ascends; the Heavenly Worthy of Salvation from Suffering descends; the Northern Culmen and Northern Dipper descend; the Upholding Sage Perfected Lord descends; the Thunder Gods of the Five Directions descend.

On the **Fifth Day**, the Southern Dipper descends; the Heavenly Peng Marshal descends.

On the **Sixth Day**, the Perfected Lord Su, Minister of the Mysterious Continent, ascends; the Heavenly Thearch tours the Eastern Well. On this day, the Jade Pivot Assembly is established to ensure peace for the month.

On the **Seventh Day**, the Western Dipper Thearch descends; the Three Primordial Ladies of the Great Simplicity pay homage to the Perfected.

On the **Eighth Day**, the Primordial Heavenly Worthy descends to the Upper Yang Palace of the Primordial Yang, convening an assembly in the Great Net Great Brahma Heaven to expound the essential methods of the *Lingbao*, delivering all sentient beings of the Three Realms and Five Paths.

On the **Ninth Day**, the Perfected Warrior descends; the Eastern Dipper descends; the Northern Yin descends; the Penglai Water Bureau Envoy descends.

On the **Tenth Day**, the Heavenly Worthy of Longevity and Life-Preservation descends.

On the **Eleventh Day**, the Heavenly Worthy of Disaster-Dispelling and Calamity-Resolving descends.

On the **Fifteenth Day**, the Primordial Heavenly Worthy tours the Jade Capital’s Upper Yang Observatory, convening an assembly of divine immortals and perfected sages of the Three Realms to expound the wondrous Dao; the Western Dipper descends.

On the **Sixteenth Day**, the Heavenly Bureau of Plunder and Excess descends.

On the **Eighteenth Day**, the Most High Lord Lao descends; the Primordial Heavenly Empress of the Grand Clarity Palace manifests; the August Earthly Thearch of the Rear Land is born.

On the **Nineteenth Day**, the Southern Dipper descends; the Sagely Attendant Perfected Lord descends; the Northern Dipper descends.

On the **Twenty-Fifth Day**, the Heavenly Chief descends.

On the **Twenty-Sixth Day**, the Sagely Attendant Perfected Lord sets forth on a tour; the Northern Dipper sets forth on a tour; the Perfected Lord Du Bing ascends as an immortal.

On the **Twenty-Seventh Day**, the Northern Culmen and Northern Dipper descend.

On the **Twenty-Eighth Day**, the Heavenly Thearch of the Great Yin and Comet manifests.

On the **Twenty-Ninth Day**, the Northern Yin descends.

On the **Second Day**, the Heavenly Thearch of Grand Simplicity and Non-Being descends.

On the **Third Day**, the Northern Culmen and Northern Dipper descend; the Sagely Attendant Perfected Lord descends.

On the **Seventh Day**, the Southern Dipper descends; the Northern Dipper descends; the Western Dipper descends; the Perfected Lord Xie of Yichun ascends as an immortal.

On the **Eighth Day**, the Day of Inaugurating Summer, the Most High Jade Clarity Great Dao Lord ascends to the Jade Empyrean and Forest Chamber of the Four Gaze Heaven; the Most High Lord Lao enters the Flowing Sands to transform the Hu; the Three Heavens’ Supreme Venerable Perfected Lord Yin is born; the Perfected Lord Ge Xiaoxian is born.

On the **Ninth Day**, the Eastern Dipper descends; the Northern Yin descends.

On the **Tenth Day**, the Heavenly Worthy of Longevity and Life-Preservation descends; the Northern Dipper sets forth on a tour.

On the **Twelfth Day**, the Great Dharma Master of the Mysterious Center descends.

On the **Thirteenth Day**, the Three August Emperors descend.

On the **Fourteenth Day**, the Perfected Lord Lü of the Purple Culmen Grotto-Heaven and Primordial Yang is born.

On the **Fifteenth Day**, the Perfected Lord of the Eastern Florescence Grotto-Heaven and Primordial Yang is born; the Western Dipper descends.

On the **Sixteenth Day**, the Heavenly Bureau of Plunder and Excess descends.

On the **Seventeenth Day**, the Sagely Attendant Perfected Lord descends.

On the **Nineteenth Day**, the Northern Yin descends.

On the **Twenty-First Day**, the Heavenly Strategist descends.

On the **Twenty-Second Day**, the Northern Dipper sets forth on a tour.

On the **Twenty-Fifth Day**, the Heavenly Chief descends.

On the **Twenty-Sixth Day**, the Sagely Attendant descends.

On the **Twenty-Seventh Day**, the Northern Culmen and Northern Dipper descend.

On the **Twenty-Eighth Day**, the Most High Lord Lao convenes an assembly of the immortals of the Three Realms and Ten Poles.

On the **Twenty-Ninth Day**, the Sagely Mother of the Northern Culmen descends.

**Fifth Month**

On the **First Day**, the Longevity-Prolonging Festival; the Most High Lord Lao transmits the Three Heavens’ Orthodox Dharma to the Celestial Master of Han; the Heavenly Thearch tours the Eastern Well; the Southern Culmen’s Perfected Lord of the Wondrous Dao of Vacuous Simplicity descends.

On the **Second Day**, the Heavenly Bureau of Plunder and Excess descends.

On the **Third Day**, the Northern Culmen and Northern Dipper descend.

On the **Fifth Day**, the Day of Life-Renewal, the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion and Salvation descends; the Heavenly Chief and Sagely Attendant Perfected Lord descend; the Perfected Warrior descends; the Northern Dipper sets forth on a tour; the Great Spirit of Sudden Fire is born; the Celestial Master Ye Daoyuan subdues the Brahmin’s demonic illusions to save Longni from peril.

On the **Sixth Day**, the Jade Pivot Assembly is established to ensure peace for the month.

On the **Ninth Day**, the Most High Jade Clarity Great Dao Lord ascends to the King Empyrean and Forest Chamber of the Four Gaze Heaven; the Eastern Dipper descends; the Northern Dipper descends.

On the **Eleventh Day**, the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion and Great Mercy universally saves all sentient beings of the Three Realms from suffering; the Heavenly Worthy of Disaster-Dispelling and Calamity-Resolving descends.

On the **Twelfth Day**, the Flesh-Tranquilizing Festival, the day when the Heavenly Perfected and Sagely Worthies manifest.

On the **Thirteenth Day**, the Sagely Attendant Perfected Lord descends; the Northern Dipper sets forth on a tour; the Perfected Lord of Reverent Tranquility manifests.

On the **Fifteenth Day**, the Most High Lord Lao manifests on Mount Heming; the Southern Culmen’s Old Star descends; the Western Dipper descends.

On the **Sixteenth Day**, the Three Primordials’ Inspectors descend.

On the **Seventeenth Day**, the Northern Dipper descends.

On the **Nineteenth Day**, the day when the qi of Heaven and Earth intermingle to transform and create the myriad things.

On the **Twentieth Day**, the Sagely Attendant descends; the Northern Dipper sets forth on a tour.

On the **Twenty-First Day**, the Heavenly Strategist descends.

On the **Twenty-Fifth Day**, the Perfected Lord of Great Peace ascends as an immortal; the Heavenly Chief Marshal descends.

On the **Twenty-Eighth Day**, the Heavenly Repose Festival; the Upper Primordial Star Lord descends; the Sagely Mother of the Northern Yin descends.

---

**Sixth Month**

On the **First Day**, the Perfected Lord of Pure Numinosity descends.

On the **Second Day**, the Heavenly Bureau of Plunder and Excess descends.

On the **Fourth Day**, the Sagely Attendant Perfected Lord descends; the Southern Dipper descends; the Northern Dipper sets forth on a tour.

On the **Fifth Day**, the Heavenly Chief descends.

On the **Sixth Day**, the Perfected Lord of Reverent Tranquility is born. On this day, the Jade Pivot Assembly is established to ensure peace for the month.

On the **Seventh Day**, the Western Dipper descends; the Perfected Warrior descends.

On the **Eighth Day**, the Sagely Attendant Perfected Lord descends; the Northern Dipper sets forth on a tour.

On the **Ninth Day**, the Eastern Dipper descends; the Southern Dipper descends; the Northern Yin descends; the Five Directions’ Thunder Gods descend.
